VExcuse me?

V<span>A talkfest is underway on how to waste rates in Orklund this week and I do not hold much hope for any progress.  Especially when I see comments like this<br /></span><span><blockquote>The really interesting issue for me is that we haven't fully quantified the problem and fully identified what it is that Wellington is hoping to achieve by the [commission]. We are still not grasping the real issue...</blockquote></span><br /><span>Interesting that a councillor elected on a red ticket is working on the premise that any final outcome needs to match what Liarbour deems needs to be achieved.  <a href="http://www.nzherald.co.nz/section/1/story.cfm?c_id=1&objectid=10490635">Why bother</a>?<br /><br />This confirms the suspected MO, that the commission is just being an excuse to head off livid ratepayers in an election year.<br /><br />Here's my view of some extremely quantifiable bits to help her on her way<br /></span><ul><li>Rates are too high</li><li>Bureaucracy at local government is rampant</li><li>8 councils to run one city is not on</li><li>Between council turf wars</li><li>Infrastructure massively underfunded</li><li>Councils playing social engineers</li><li>Cost plus regime for ratepayers using services they have already paid for<br /></li></ul>and the fix<br /><ul><li>Major infrastructure should be fully funded from central government</li><li>One council to run the whole city, ending parochial wars</li><li>Wield a knife in the bureaucracy</li><li>Gut social engineering and public transport from local government</li><li>Arterial roading to be fully funded from central government<br /></li><li>Council to stick to managing parks, local roads, local water/sewerage, rubbish collection</li><li>Ditch all rates input into sports stadia and the like</li><li>Stop the twin-cities waste of rates</li><li>One set of rules for all cultures</li><li>No second airport<br /></li></ul>Unfortunately, I suspect my grandchildren will be having this same discussion.  It has been going on for 4 decades that I know of and still has not been addresssed.

VCo-Browsing with Clavardon
p31
sg5
Vhttp://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/readwriteweb/~3/229900226/cobrowsing_with_clavardon.php
p32
sg13
(lp33
sg15
V<img src="http://farm3.static.flickr.com/2031/2244575587_ce6fa6dfb4_o.gif" />Clavardon, from the French for "to chat," is the latest from Canadian-based \u000Acompany <a href="http://www.sosign.com/">Sosign</a>. The product, launched in late 2007,&nbsp; is a tool for co-browsing \u000Aof e-commerce web sites, which means it's essentially another way to do social \u000Ashopping. However, unlike some other social shopping services, <a href="http://www.clavardon.com/">Clavardon</a> is a tool \u000Athat adds a layer to any existing web site to provide the co-browsing \u000Afunctionality. The solution offers some unique features that provide real-time \u000Ainteraction between its users. Shoppers can co-browse with each other or with the \u000Aweb site's sales manager in the virtual store.  \u000A\u000A<p>In this way, Clavardon is more like a live support solution, but one that \u000Aoffers more functionality than most. The tool offers the ability for users to \u000Aco-browse and chat with each other, but it also offers things like co-scrolling, \u000Awhere user's can control each other's interaction on a page, co-highlighting, \u000Awhere one user could highlight a section of the page for the others to see, and \u000Ajoint form filling, where different users can input information into the same \u000Aform. \u000A</p><p>This type of interaction could be useful for those who want to shop together, \u000Abut it seems like it may be even more useful to promote interaction between site \u000Aowners and visitors. In this way, the service is not only beneficial to general \u000Aconsumers who want to shop with their friends, but it could also be utilized in a \u000Abusiness environment. \u000A</p><p>It's easy to imagine site owners using the tool to provide instructional \u000Atours or training to their new customers on how to use their web site. For \u000Aexample, an office supply company could demonstrate how to use search, shopping \u000Alists, and checkout to all the office managers in a particular company at the \u000Asame time. The visitors could respond with feedback and questions as the \u000Ainstruction was provided, leading to a better comprehension of what a particular \u000Acompany's web site had to offer.</p>\u000A<p><img src="http://farm3.static.flickr.com/2112/2245368958_411a520f8b_o.png" /></p><p>The tool is a solely commercial product that is marketed to e-commerce site \u000Aowners at a base price of $199 per month. This allows for an unlimited number of \u000Ausers and up to 500 sessions per month. A 15-day free trial version is available \u000A<a href="http://www.clavardon.com/order.en.html?package=0">here</a> or you can get a taste of what Clavardon is like by trying the <a href="http://www.clavardon.com/demo.en.html">online demo</a>. \u000A</p><p>Since the tool is so good for providing live support, the "shop with friends" \u000Aaspect seems to be more of a secondary feature. Although possible, there are \u000A<a href="http://www.readwriteweb.com/archives/social_shopping_faceoff.php">plenty of other social shopping services</a> that provide more features in that \u000Aarea. \u000A</p><p>However, live support and chat features are incredibly useful in today's \u000Afast-paced world where we don't have time to wait for an email back from \u000Asupport. A tool like Clavardon improves upon the live support offerings that are \u000Aalready available to allow for a more personalized and social experience. That \u000Aalone makes the product notable and worth a look. </p>\u000A<p><a href="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~a/readwriteweb?a=0Tg3uU"><img src="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~a/readwriteweb?i=0Tg3uU" border="0" /></a></p><div class="feedflare">\u000A<a href="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~f/readwriteweb?a=4pFAudE"><img src="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~f/readwriteweb?i=4pFAudE" border="0" /></a> <a href="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~f/readwriteweb?a=lHlbhME"><img src="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~f/readwriteweb?i=lHlbhME" border="0" /></a> <a href="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~f/readwriteweb?a=z0PbG8e"><img src="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~f/readwriteweb?i=z0PbG8e" border="0" /></a> <a href="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~f/readwriteweb?a=LKiOlre"><img src="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~f/readwriteweb?i=LKiOlre" border="0" /></a> <a href="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~f/readwriteweb?a=rhYQrOe"><img src="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~f/readwriteweb?i=rhYQrOe" border="0" /></a> <a href="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~f/readwriteweb?a=lxcFCoE"><img src="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~f/readwriteweb?i=lxcFCoE" border="0" /></a> <a href="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~f/readwriteweb?a=YxgQT2E"><img src="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~f/readwriteweb?i=YxgQT2E" border="0" /></a>\u000A</div><img src="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/readwriteweb/~4/229900226" height="1" width="1" />

VClimate change: a strapped chicken
p45
sg5
Vhttp://norightturn.blogspot.com/2008/02/climate-change-strapped-chicken.html
p46
sg13
(lp47
sg15
V<p>DPF <a href="http://www.kiwiblog.co.nz/2008/02/the_cost_of_carbon_mitigation.html">makes a lot of noise</a> about a <a href="http://www.nzbr.org.nz/documents/features/NZBR%20PEPANZ%20Carbon%20Mitigation%20Scenarios.pdf">Business Round Table-commissioned study</a> [PDF] which claims that reducing greenhouse gas emissions to 1990 levels by 2025 would <a href="http://www.nzherald.co.nz/feature/story.cfm?c_id=26&objectid=10490750&ref=rss">"cost each household $19,000 a year"</a>.  DPF regards this as proof positive that the costs of mitigation are too high, and that therefore we should not bother at all to do anything about emissions.  Meanwhile, Hot Topic looks at the report and finds that it is a <a href="http://hot-topic.co.nz/2008/02/05/they-would-say-that-again-wouldnt-they/">strapped chicken</a>:\u000A<blockquote>\u000A<i>But, as is usual with these things, when you look at the assumptions that underpin the forecast, you find that they have been carefully designed to produce the result the sponsors wanted. Take a look at the method used (see PDF linked above): they define a \u201Cbusiness as usual\u201D case against which they will measure the costs of emissions reductions - and they shoot for GDP growth of 4.5 - 5% per annum. I don\u2019t have the figures to hand, but I can\u2019t think of any period in the recent past when GDP growth has been that high - and certainly not for 17 successive years. And the costs? They use very high carbon prices (up to $300/tonne). So, when you artificially inflate both long term growth and the costs of action, you discover that action\u2019s expensive.\u000A\u000A<p>Why am I not surprised?</i>\u000A</blockquote>\u000A\u000AThis is a classic spindoctor's trick - assume fantasy growth rates, then let the miracle of compound interest do its work - so its no real surprise that the spindoctor has fallen for it.  But the idea that this would be considered credible in the real world is just laughable.  \u000A\u000A<p>For those who are interested, the difference between the BRT's "business as usual" growth scenario of 4.9% per year and a more realistic one of 3% (the trend for the last decade, widely considered to be the best long run of growth New Zealand has had since the 60's, so probably too high on average) is about 27% of final economic output.  Which is pretty much their "result" right there.\u000A\u000A<p><i>Update:</i> I have misrepresented DPF in this post; see my <a href="http://norightturn.blogspot.com/2008/02/correction-and-apology.html">correction and apology</a>.

V<a href="http://bp0.blogger.com/_Qy4iftwk5JM/R6dYgNUzXgI/AAAAAAAACik/ZHuBTnrSqXs/s1600-h/trev.jpg"><img src="http://bp0.blogger.com/_Qy4iftwk5JM/R6dYgNUzXgI/AAAAAAAACik/ZHuBTnrSqXs/s400/trev.jpg" border="0" alt="" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5163192808159534594" /></a><br /><b>breakfast news comment</b><br /><a href="http://www.stuff.co.nz/4387090a11.html">Mallard plays down fuss over Myanmar contract</a><br /><i>Telecommunications company Kordia should have told the Government it was doing business in Myanmar, but the lapse was understandable, State Owned Enterprise Minister Trevor Mallard said yesterday. The National Party has criticised the Government stance over the state-owned broadcast and telecommunications business's contract in military-ruled Myanmar.<br />National foreign affairs spokesman Murray McCully said it was contradictory that the Government had no problem with Kordia's contract when it had "tantrums" over Air New Zealand carrying Australian troops to the Iraq war.</i><br /><br />Hmmm, couple of things \u2013 Trev it is slightly hypercritical, and your claim that it\u2019s okay because there are no current economic sanctions against Myanmar isn\u2019t any defence, other countries have placed sanctions, so should we. Murray \u2013 mate, you the Dark Lord of the Sith complaining about ethics and hypocrisy? Oh come on, how did you keep a straight face during that interview on TV? Interestingly enough, in a Freakonomics kinda way, once mobile phone use reaches 15% of a population it is very difficult for dictatorships to keep control of a population as the transfer of independent news and information cancels out the power of state created media.

V<p><img src="http://www.readwriteweb.com/images/mowserlogo.jpg" />Telephony-head Russell Beattie added an <a href="http://m.mowser.com/mp3/portishead">MP3 search and download feature</a> to his mobile service <em>Mowser</em> tonight, powered by music search engine <a href="http://www.seeqpod.com/">SeeqPod</a>.  The service makes it remarkably easy to search for, download and listen to any song online.   All. From. Your. Phone.  It's nice.</p>\u000A\u000A<p>This is just one of a number of "powered by SeeqPod" announcements you'll likely be seeing if you are interested in music search.  Josh Lowensohn <a href="http://music.download.com/8301-5_32-9864445-13.html?part=rss&tag=feed&subj=Crossfade">reported on yet another</a>, called <a href="http://songerize.com/">Songerize</a>, today.  Enjoy the music and the API action while you can, because SeeqPod is too good to be true and is headed for court.</p>\u000A\u000A<p>It turns out that <a href="http://www.seeqpod.com/blog/?p=19">Warner Music Group is suing SeeqPod</a>.  As Mike Miner blogs at <a href="http://www.tvo.org/cfmx/tvoorg/theagenda/index.cfm?page_id=3&action=blog&subaction=viewpost&blog_id=81&post_id=6766&CFID=168467&CFTOKEN=25327961">The Agenda</a>:<br />\u000A<blockquote>Maybe it's just too beautiful to live. Warner Music Group is suing Seeqpod, the finest music site I've seen on the internet, because it allows people to scour the net for music, put it in a playlist and play it for free. Naturally, not all the music files it finds has dotted all its copyright i's or crossed many legal t's.</blockquote></p>\u000A\u000A<p>For now, if you're looking for a good web page mobilizer - much less an mobile MP3 search engine, check out <a href="http://m.mowser.com">Mowser</a>.  If you're unfamiliar with <a href="http://seeqpod.com">SeeqPod</a> - here's a taste below.</p>\u000A\u000A<center><br /><a href="http://www.seeqpod.com/search">SeeqPod - Playable Search</a></center>\u000A<p><a href="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~a/readwriteweb?a=9SKESF"><img src="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~a/readwriteweb?i=9SKESF" border="0" /></a></p><div class="feedflare">\u000A<a href="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~f/readwriteweb?a=7KJq0IE"><img src="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~f/readwriteweb?i=7KJq0IE" border="0" /></a> <a href="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~f/readwriteweb?a=wDktxzE"><img src="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~f/readwriteweb?i=wDktxzE" border="0" /></a> <a href="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~f/readwriteweb?a=XfeXmAe"><img src="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~f/readwriteweb?i=XfeXmAe" border="0" /></a> <a href="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~f/readwriteweb?a=hPZbe7e"><img src="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~f/readwriteweb?i=hPZbe7e" border="0" /></a> <a href="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~f/readwriteweb?a=XkCSIae"><img src="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~f/readwriteweb?i=XkCSIae" border="0" /></a> <a href="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~f/readwriteweb?a=xAj1a1E"><img src="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~f/readwriteweb?i=xAj1a1E" border="0" /></a> <a href="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~f/readwriteweb?a=chwhkDE"><img src="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~f/readwriteweb?i=chwhkDE" border="0" /></a>\u000A</div><img src="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/readwriteweb/~4/229337896" height="1" width="1" />

V<a href="http://www.fishpond.co.nz/product_info.php?ref=797&products_id=4626642&affiliate_banner_id=1"><img src="http://bp3.blogger.com/_HZlxBZQcoGI/R6jpO-8WwnI/AAAAAAAABgA/1eyD-1an2kA/s320/victoria_me_or_the_dog.jpg" alt="" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5163633416403862130" border="0" /></a>Tubby dogs come under the watchful eye of dog training expert Victoria Stilwell in tonight's special episode of <span>It's Me or The Dog: Fat Dog Special</span>.<br /><br />According to Victoria over-feeding a dog is just as neglectful as not feeding one. That will come as a shock to doting pet lovers who like to overfeed their dog with treats and leftovers!<br /><br />In <span>It's Me Or The Dog: Fat Dog Special</span>, Victoria's got her sights set on transforming three porky pooches into honed hounds. There's Hattie, the huge Beagle who steals food from the bins and kitchen counter. Next up is Gizmo, the chunky Chihuahua whose owner dotes on him so much that she hand-feeds her little darling Indian takeaways and chocolates. Lastly, there's Jess the dumpy Daschund whose belly is dragging along the floor and whose owner is dragging her heels when it comes to changing her dog's diet.<br /><br />With advice on diet and exercise, as well as medical implications from vet Marc Abrahams, Victoria has to make these owners see the damage they are doing to their pets, before it's too late. Other pet weight loss shows include<br /><ul><li>Even My Pet's A Porker (currently screening on TV2), hosted by nutritionist and naturopath Lani Lopez, and 'The Pet Doctor', veterinarian Seton Butler</li><li><a href="http://www.nzrealitytv.com/search/label/Downsize%20My%20Pet">Downsize My Pet</a></li><li><a href="http://www.nzrealitytv.com/2007/07/evil-diet-witch-wants-people-and-pets.html">Evil Diet Witch</a> (in production)</li></ul><br />TVNZ are <a href="http://tvnz.co.nz/view/comp_skin/1570728" target="_blank">giving away copies of Victoria Stilwell's books</a> <a href="http://www.fishpond.co.nz/product_info.php?ref=797&products_id=4626642&affiliate_banner_id=1">It's Me Or The Dog</a>  and <a href="http://www.fishpond.co.nz/product_info.php?ref=797&products_id=4626642&affiliate_banner_id=1">It's Me Or The Dog: Fat Dog Slim</a>. Unfortunately, there is something wrong with the TVNZ entry form but you have until 12th March to enter, so I suggest you check back in a couple of days.\u000A<p><a href="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~a/NewZealandRealityTv?a=crgsff"><img src="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~a/NewZealandRealityTv?i=crgsff" border="0" /></a></p><div class="feedflare">\u000A<a href="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~f/NewZealandRealityTv?a=SASnq9E"><img src="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~f/NewZealandRealityTv?i=SASnq9E" border="0" /></a> <a href="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~f/NewZealandRealityTv?a=dnz9J5e"><img src="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~f/NewZealandRealityTv?i=dnz9J5e" border="0" /></a> <a href="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~f/NewZealandRealityTv?a=BOnnUpe"><img src="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~f/NewZealandRealityTv?i=BOnnUpe" border="0" /></a> <a href="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~f/NewZealandRealityTv?a=lFDhxde"><img src="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~f/NewZealandRealityTv?i=lFDhxde" border="0" /></a>\u000A</div><img src="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/NewZealandRealityTv/~4/229884394" height="1" width="1" />

VKeeping Tabs on Super Tuesday
p125
sg5
Vhttp://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/readwriteweb/~3/229715659/keeping_tabs_on_super_tuesday.php
p126
sg13
(lp127
sg15
V<p><img border="0" src="http://www.readwriteweb.com/images/vote-button.jpg" width="100" height="99" />Today is so-called "<a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Super_Duper_Tuesday">Super Tuesday</a>" in the US.  Voters in 24 states are heading to the polls -- including in large population states like New York, California, and Illinois -- to decide who get to face off for the job of US president as the nominees of the Republican and Democratic parties.  After the votes have been counted tonight, 52% of the Democratic and 41% of the Republican delegates will have been awarded, and it may be that we have a clearer picture of who those nominees are.</p>\u000A\u000A<p>Following election returns from 24 states can be overwhelming, though.  Certainly it is interesting and it can be a lot of fun (especially for political junkies), but that's a lot of data to absorb in a very short time.  Thankfully, there are a number of tools on the web to make election watching easier.  Below are some of our favorites.</p>\u000A\u000A<h2><a href="http://www.cnn.com/ELECTION/2008/">CNN Election Center 2008</a></h2>\u000A\u000A<p>In our opinion, CNN has by far the slickest and easiest to navigate election site out of all the major mainstream news media sources.  They have a well designed, easy to navigate, and clearly laid out page that puts a wealth of information at your fingertips, including live election results, delegate counts, entrance and exit polls, candidate overviews, money charts, and general election info.  If you're looking for just the straight state-by-state results, <a href="http://content.usatoday.com/news/politics/election2008/results-all.aspx">USA Today</a> does a great job.</a></p>\u000A\u000A<h2><a href="http://politweets.com/">Politweets</a></h2>\u000A\u000A<p>Politweets is our favorite Twitter politics mashup.  <a href="http://www.readwriteweb.com/archives/politweets_twittering_politics.php">Last month</a> we said that, "For political junkies, Politweet will be a must monitor web-site on every primary date this season until we know who the candidates for the general election are."  Assuming Twitter can keep the lights on, Politweets will again be a must watch site throughout the day. Also check out the <a href="http://twitter.com/SuperTuesday">SuperTuesday</a> Twitter stream from the <a href="http://www.virtualvantagepoints.com/">Virtual Vantage Points</a> blog.</p> \u000A\u000A<h2><a href="http://googleblog.blogspot.com/2008/02/be-part-of-super-tuesday-action.html">Google Super Tuesday Map</a></h2>\u000A\u000A<p>In an effort to make sure Twitter goes down, Google has also teamed up with the service to create a maps mashup that shows Twitter updates about the primaries as they come in from across the country.  It will display election results down to the county level after the returns are in, as well.  The Google News team also slapped together an election gadget so you can embed  state-by-state results on your web page.</p>\u000A\u000A<p><img border="0" src="http://www.readwriteweb.com/images/google-suptuesmap.jpg" width="610" height="420" /></p>\u000A\u000A<h2><a href="http://www.youtube.com/supertuesday">YouTube YouChoose Super Tuesday</a></h2>\u000A\u000A<p>YouTube has a Google Maps mashup of their own that will aggregate and post geolocated videos throughout the day from candidates, news organizations, and YouTubers.  The coverage isn't really restricted to Super Tuesday states, but it is still worth checking out -- many times the citizen journalist view is clearer than the one you get via mainstream sources.</p>\u000A\u000A<h2><a href="http://think.mtv.com/Issues/politics/">MTV Choose or Lose Street Team</a></h2>\u000A\u000A<p>Speaking of citizen journalism, MTV's Street Team has citizen journalists dispatched to 23 Super Tuesday states to upload live and recorded mobile videos and blog posts throughout the day (absent is a representative from West Virginia, whose primary is actually May 13 -- the Republican party is awarding some delegates today via a statewide convention, however).  Last week we called MTV's online election coverage a <a href="http://www.readwriteweb.com/archives/mtv_election_coverage_citizen_journalism.php">coup for citizen journalism</a>.</p>\u000A\u000A<h2><a href="http://www.newsweek.com/id/94616">Newsweek Live Webcast: Inside Super Tuesday</a></h2>\u000A\u000A<p>If mainstream journalism is more your thing, then Newsweek has you covered on the web.  The magazine, along with owner the Wasington Post, is trotting out the heavy hitters for six continuous hours of live streaming web video coverage.  Bob Woodward, Ben Bradlee, Sally Quinn, Howard Kurtz, and Leonard Downie will participate, with Newsweek editor Jon Meacham anchoring from Washingtonpost.com's headquarters in Arlington, Virginia.   WaPo and Newsweek reporters Michael Isikoff, Howard Fineman, Jonathan Alter, and others, including those from online magazine Slate, will contribute reports throughout the evening.  Newsweek's operation is aiming to bring the name appeal and polish of broadcast news to the web.  We'll see if it works.</p>\u000A\u000A<h2><a href="http://www.memeorandum.com/">Memeorandum</a></h2>\u000A\u000A<p>From the maker of Techmeme, Gabe Rivera's political memetracker keeps a pulse on the political blogosphere.  It's a safe bet everyone will be buzzing about Super Tuesday today, but what are the individual storylines that will no doubt permeate the coverage?  Following the related and discussion links on Memeorandum will let you find out.  For a broader view of what people are talking about on the blogosphere, check out <a href="http://www.politicaltrends.info/">PoliticalTrends.info</a>.</p>\u000A<p><a href="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~a/readwriteweb?a=c2l7jU"><img src="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~a/readwriteweb?i=c2l7jU" border="0" /></a></p><div class="feedflare">\u000A<a href="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~f/readwriteweb?a=ozKIxiE"><img src="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~f/readwriteweb?i=ozKIxiE" border="0" /></a> <a href="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~f/readwriteweb?a=1pwN6fE"><img src="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~f/readwriteweb?i=1pwN6fE" border="0" /></a> <a href="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~f/readwriteweb?a=hZT1wYe"><img src="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~f/readwriteweb?i=hZT1wYe" border="0" /></a> <a href="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~f/readwriteweb?a=PC2SQqe"><img src="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~f/readwriteweb?i=PC2SQqe" border="0" /></a> <a href="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~f/readwriteweb?a=cpYv7ye"><img src="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~f/readwriteweb?i=cpYv7ye" border="0" /></a> <a href="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~f/readwriteweb?a=E5oYsAE"><img src="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~f/readwriteweb?i=E5oYsAE" border="0" /></a> <a href="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~f/readwriteweb?a=VenE8oE"><img src="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~f/readwriteweb?i=VenE8oE" border="0" /></a>\u000A</div><img src="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/readwriteweb/~4/229715659" height="1" width="1" />

V<p>My recent experiences in <a href="http://jimdonovan.net.nz/2008/02/05/dont-call-me-ill-call-you/" title="Don't call me; I'll call you" target="_blank">opening, transferring</a> and <a href="http://jimdonovan.net.nz/2008/01/25/how-to-close-a-customer-account-nicely/" title="How to close a customer account nicely" target="_blank">closing accounts</a> reminded me of something I learnt several decades ago:</p>\u000A<ul>\u000A<li>Rule 1: make it easy for the customer to give you their business!</li>\u000A<li>Rule 2: make it easy for the customer to keep on giving you their business!</li>\u000A<li>Rule 3: When the customer stops giving you their business (whatever the reason), still make it easy, so they might want to come back to you again!</li>\u000A</ul>\u000A<img src="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/JDEnAvant/~4/229373619" height="1" width="1" />

VHeadphones and the tube
p165
sg5
Vhttp://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/TheChickenCoop/~3/229591216/HeadphonesAndTheTube.aspx
p166
sg13
(lp167
sg15
VSo, no surprise here, I travel to work\u000Aon the tube. It's fantastic - especially all the sub-second glimpses of things I get\u000Aas we fly past some likely forgotten station or mainenance area. It still captivates\u000Ame. (offtopic: anyone know of an underground tour of London?)<br /><br />\u000AHowever, the tube is two things: noisey and dirty. Dirty I can handle - blow my nose\u000Awhen I get out, and I'm sorted, tho I'm told being in the tube for 2 hours a day (which\u000AI am) is like <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/London_Underground_air_pollution">smoking\u000Aa cigarette or three</a>. Oh, well. I think I can live with that.<br /><br />\u000AThe noise polution, however, is something else. It's LOUD in there. So loud, that\u000Awith the usual iPod headphones (which let in a lot of external noise), I have to crank\u000Athe volume up to almost 100%. When I'm not in the tube, this volume is close to unbareable.\u000AThrow in a RPM session at the gym at work, and my ears are ringing by the end of the\u000Aday.<br /><br />\u000AI own a pair of Blackbox M14's, which I use mostly when I'm on planes or in an aircon'ed\u000Aoffice, as the noise cancelling is really good. However, they are not really suitable\u000Afor use on the tube - they are large, obvious, and not overly portable. So I went\u000Ahunting for a replacement pair.<br /><br />\u000AThe options I came up with were:<br /><ul><li>\u000AA pair of C14's from blackbox. I dont like earbuds with attached circuit boxes, so\u000Athey were removed from the list quickly - same with other makes with the same setup.\u000AThey are around $170 NZ, which is around 60£. So the price is good....</li><li>\u000ASee what I can find in the apple store.</li></ul>\u000ASo, I took option #2. Actually, I wanted to see if they had the Macbook Air in the\u000Astore (they dont), and I have to go thru Oxford Circus anyway to get home, and the\u000Aapple store is about 100m from the tube enterance.... (cue self-justification now)<br /><br />\u000AAfter looking around, there were various ones in my price range - Sennheiser, Bose\u000A(well, just out of my price range), Shure, JBL, and a few others. They come in three\u000A"formats" - clip on's which sit ON the ear; clipons which sit IN the ear, and buds\u000Awhich sit IN the ear. As I wanted to eliminate the outside noise, the IN the ear ones\u000Awere the best option. I would have gone for the Shure above any of the others, excep\u000Athe price is crazy. 170-350£!? WTF! Rod loves his, but sadly I dont (yet) have his\u000Abank balance.<br /><br /><img src="http://www.harmanaudio.com/images/products/front_large/JBLREF220BLK-H.jpg" height="240" width="320" /><br /><br />\u000ATo cut a short story shorter, I went for the JBL's - <a href="http://www.jbl.com/home/products/product_detail.aspx?prod=JBLREF220BLK-H&Language=ENG&Country=GB&Region=EUROPE&cat=MME&ser=HMM&featureid=12362">the\u000A220 Reference model</a> to be specific (<a href="http://store.apple.com/Apple/WebObjects/ukstore.woa/wa/RSLID?mco=4B9033F6&nplm=TL122">£50\u000Aat the Apple Store</a>). They are small, black (which means I'm not screaming "I have\u000Aan ipod!"), sit in the ear canal and block out almost ALL external noise, and come\u000Awith wrap-around-the-ear bits, as well as being free-standing. Why does no-one else\u000Ado this? This means I can have them as normal ear buds when I'm on the tube (most\u000Aof the time), but have them held onto my ears when I'm at the gym. Best of both worlds.<br /><br />\u000AThe best thing about them is that now <b>I can have the volume at around 40%</b> and\u000Ahear it clearly on the tube. Before, <b>it was at around 90-100%</b>. Even after just\u000Aone day of using them, the ringing in my ears is calming down. And thats gotta be\u000Agood for me.<br /><p></p><br /><hr />\u000A[ <a href="http://flickr.com/photos/nicwise">Flickr Photos</a> | <a href="http://www.linkedin.com/in/nicwise">LinkedIn\u000AProfile</a> ]<br />\u000AThe opinions in this blog are mine. No-one else wants them anyway! \u000A<div class="feedflare">\u000A<a href="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~f/TheChickenCoop?a=qTaQ1mE"><img src="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~f/TheChickenCoop?i=qTaQ1mE" border="0" /></a> <a href="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~f/TheChickenCoop?a=abtEwqE"><img src="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~f/TheChickenCoop?i=abtEwqE" border="0" /></a> <a href="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~f/TheChickenCoop?a=mt5Vtbe"><img src="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~f/TheChickenCoop?i=mt5Vtbe" border="0" /></a>\u000A</div><img src="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/TheChickenCoop/~4/229591216" height="1" width="1" />

VThey would say that (again), wouldn\u2019t they?
p193
sg5
Vhttp://hot-topic.co.nz/2008/02/05/they-would-say-that-again-wouldnt-they/
p194
sg13
(lp195
sg15
V<p><a href="http://hot-topic.co.nz/wp-content/uploads/2008/02/dinosaur-roar.jpg"><img src="http://hot-topic.co.nz/wp-content/uploads/2008/02/dinosaur-roar-tm.jpg" width="129" height="100" alt="dinosaur_roar.jpeg" class="left" /></a> There are times when specially commissioned economic forecasts are a useful contribution to debate on emissions reductions, and times when they are not. The latest, commissioned by the Business Roundtable and the Petroleum Exploration and Production Association (Pepanz) from Adolf Stroombergen at Infometrics, is a fine example of the latter. The numbers allow Roger Kerr to rumble ominously [<a href="http://www.stuff.co.nz/4388528a13.html" target="_top">Stuff</a>, <span><a href="http://www.nzherald.co.nz/feature/story.cfm?c_id=26&objectid=10490750&ref=rss" target="_top">Herald</a></span>, original BR press release (<a href="http://www.nzbr.org.nz/documents/releases/0204CarbonNeutralityMR.pdf">PDF</a>)]:</p>\u000A<blockquote><p>\u000A  <span>"The impact on numerous industries would be devastating - reductions in output of the order of 30 per cent to 40 per cent are reported in the case of sheep and dairy farming - and major industrial firms could face complete closure," Mr Kerr said.</span>\u000A</p></blockquote>\u000A<p>Even worse, households could be $19,000 a year worse off by 2025 and the government would still fail to meet a notional target of reducing emissions to 1990 levels by 2025. Sounds dire. Better do nothing&nbsp;then...</p>\u000A<p>But, as is usual with these things, when you look at the assumptions that underpin the forecast, you find that they have been carefully designed to produce the result the sponsors wanted. Take a look at the method used (see PDF linked above): they define a "business as usual" case against which they will measure the costs of emissions reductions - and they shoot for GDP growth of 4.5 - 5% per annum. I don't have the figures to hand, but I can't think of any period in the recent past when GDP growth has been that high - and certainly not for 17 successive years. And the costs? They use very high carbon prices (up to $300/tonne). So, when you artificially inflate both long term growth and the costs of action, you discover that action's&nbsp;expensive.</p>\u000A<p>Why am I not&nbsp;surprised?</p>\u000A<p>And I'm not entirely surprised by news (<a href="http://www.radionz.co.nz/news/latest/200802041834/iwi_leaders_oppose_climate-change_bill" target="_top">Radio NZ</a>) that 15 iwi leaders, chaired by Tuku Morgan and meeting at the Waitangi Treaty grounds say they oppose all climate-change legislation - because it has no regard for Treaty rights. But I'd like to know more about why. Forestry interests are one thing, geothermal sensitivies another, but what are the Treaty&nbsp;implications?</p>

VThe tragedy of the foreshore and seabed
p207
sg5
Vhttp://norightturn.blogspot.com/2008/02/tragedy-of-foreshore-and-seabed.html
p208
sg13
(lp209
sg15
V<p>The government has <a href="http://www.nzherald.co.nz/section/1/story.cfm?c_id=1&objectid=10490754">signed a deal with Ngati Porou to recognise their territorial customary rights over the foreshore and seabed in their tribal rohe</a>.  While I <a href="http://norightturn.blogspot.com/2004/11/final-words-on-foreshore-and-seabed.html">opposed</a> the Foreshore and Seabed Act as an attack on due process and equality under the law, I still think this is good news.  At the same time, it also demonstrates perfectly the tragedy of the foreshore and seabed.  \u000A<blockquote>\u000A<i>When the agreement is finalised, it will require legal recognition of Ngati Porou's territorial customary rights.\u000A\u000A<p>The agreement will ensure Ngati Porou's status is recorded in official documents and is taken into account in consent processes under the Resource Management Act and Marine Reserves Act.\u000A\u000A<p>It will also require the Government to consult with Ngati Porou on issues such as fisheries and conservation in the East Cape coastal area.\u000A\u000A<p>There will also be a protection for specified customary rights and the ability to block resource consents which would affect the coastal customary rights areas.\u000A\u000A<p>The Government and the iwi are yet finalise details of the agreement including the location of territorial customary rights areas and the collection of evidence to back the claims.</i>\u000A</blockquote>\u000A\u000AReading this, the overwhelming feeling is that this is exactly the sort of settlement crown and iwi would have been discussing if the law had not been passed and iwi had been free to contest ownership through the courts.  So instead of having a few court cases short-circuited by negotiation and mutual settlement, we've had them short-circuited by law and a denial of fundamental human rights - with consequent feelings of betrayal and mistrust - to achieve pretty much the same result.  In what universe could that possibly be considered a good outcome?\u000A\u000A<p>By legislating in panic, the government has made its job harder.  Not only does it have to reach the same settlements it would have reached anyway; it also has to deal with the legacy of mistrust it has created.  We're all going to be paying for that mistake for some time to come.

VObama and Paul: The Kings of the Web Election
p219
sg5
Vhttp://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/readwriteweb/~3/229682770/obama_and_paul_the_kings_of_the_web_election.php
p220
sg13
(lp221
sg15
V<p><img border="0" src="http://www.readwriteweb.com/images/ballot-box.jpg" width="110" height="113" />There's no question this year that Barack Obama and Ron Paul are the kings of US politics on the Internet.  They both command the <a href="http://blog.compete.com/election2008/">lion's share of their party's attention</a> online and seem to dominate social networking and social media sites.  So why is only one of those campaigns actually working?  How come only Obama has been able to translate his online success to success at the polls?  We thought we'd take a brief look today at the Obama campaign and why it has been successful, while citizens in 24 US states head to the polls as part of "Super Tuesday."</p>\u000A<p><i><b>UPDATE:</b> Also check out <b><a href="http://www.readwriteweb.com/archives/keeping_tabs_on_super_tuesday.php">Keeping Tabs on Super Tuesday</a></b>, our guide to following Super Tuesday via the Internet.</i></p>\u000A\u000A<p>Last week Obama's campaign announced that it had raised $32 million in January alone, a <a href="http://blog.washingtonpost.com/the-trail/2008/02/01/obama_sets_new_online_record.html">record $28 million</a> online -- more than Howard Dean raised in his entire 2004 campaign.  Twice this campaign cycle, Ron Paul has set <a href="http://blog.washingtonpost.com/the-trail/2007/12/16/ron_paul_beats_own_fundraising.html?hpid=topnews">single day fundraising records</a>.   If anything, the power of online fundraising has been proved many times over during this election.</p>\u000A\u000A<p>Looking over Obama's numbers, we see that an overwhelming amount of that $28 million was via small donations -- 90% under $100 each.  10,000 people gave between $5 and $10.  That's a whole new paradigm for fundraising.  Rather than chase $2,300 checks from a few hundred rich people at lavish fundraisers (okay, they still do that), campaigns can more easily focus on collecting thousands of smaller donations from regular people that add up to the same amount (or more).</p>\u000A\u000A<p>Further, 10,000 donations under $10 means the email addresses of 10,000 people who can still give more money later.  About half of Hilary Clinton's money came from "maxed out" voters compared to just about one third for Obama.  That gives Obama a much larger pool of donors to hit up for more cash and to put on notice for get out the vote campaigns.</p>\u000A\u000A<p>Though I am loathe to agree with Karl Rove, he's right about how the Internet is <a href="http://online.wsj.com/article/SB120173791597330347.html?mod=hpp_us_insid">affecting campaign fundraising</a>.  "The Internet dramatically shortens the gap between political success and raising money," he wrote. "Today, if you do well in a debate on Tuesday night you can begin raising large sums of money Wednesday morning. Effective fundraising can be a mouse-click away."</p>\u000A\u000A<p>That's something that nearly all of the campaigns are doing.  Within hours after Obama's win in South Carolina, his campaign had dispatched emails to supporters pitching for donations.  However, raising money doesn't win elections.  "Raising the most amount of money by no means assures you of winning the presidential primary," <a href="http://www.dailyherald.com/story/?id=127039&src=117">says former chairman</a> of the Federal Election Commission Michael Toner.  And for Paul, money and online popularity hasn't translated into votes.  For Obama, though, arguably his online success has had an impact at the polls.</p>\u000A\u000A<p>The reason may be in get out the vote efforts of each party.  Both Paul and Obama, with their anti-war stances and Internet savvy, are attractive to young voters.  But only the Democrats are succeeding in getting young people to the voting booths.  In Iowa, exit polls showed 40% of voters under the age of 44, and Obama killed in those demographics.  On the Republican side, just 26% of voters were under 44.  That picture was repeated in other early primary states.</p>\u000A\u000A<p>Incidentally, this is also potentially the reason that Mike Huckabee has faded as well -- he appeals to young people with, as one <a href="http://www.thestate.com/447/story/293548.html">South Carolina paper writes</a>, "his celebrity supporters, preacher\u2019s gift for humor and skill with an electric guitar."</p>\u000A\u000A<p>The Democrats are succeeding with young people because they are targeting young people and they are using the Internet to successfully microtarget and rally their base.  The Obama campaign, for example, uses <a href="http://techpresident.com/blog/entry/21119/is_the_obama_campaign_a_model_for_online_politics">sophisticated targeting tools</a> that let them send specially tailored campaign materials to each voter.  Firm supporters get a different email than those on the fence.</p>\u000A\u000A<p>Other progressive organizations are using similar tools.  One is called <a href="http://catalist.us/">Catalist</a>.  It is used by large progressive organizations like MoveOn and the AFL-CIO to microtarget their campaigns. According to Tony DeYoung of Catalyst Resources (unrelated to Catalist -- Catalyst is a design firm that was contracted by Catalist to redesign the UI of their "Q-Tool" software), Catalist utilizes "on-demand data analysis services to help Democratics microtarget in their voter outreach efforts. Microtargeting uses sophisticated computer models regularly used in commercial marketing, which helps campaigns to locate sympathetic voters and target them with individually tailored messages on issues that are predicted to be most important to them."</p>\u000A\u000A<p>This is the same technique the Republicans employed to great effect in 2004 to get out messages to conservative evangelical Christian voters -- who this election cycle don't have a clear cut favorite among the front runners.  Which may explain why their get out the vote efforts aren't working as well this time around.</p>\u000A\u000A<p>So while both Obama and Paul are running effective online campaigns, albeit in different ways, the get out the vote efforts of the Democrats, which target young people, play to Obama's strength.  While strong turnout by voters over the age of 45 have played to John McCain on the Republican side.</p>\u000A\u000A<p><b>Related:</b> <a href="http://www.readwriteweb.com/archives/keeping_tabs_on_super_tuesday.php">Keeping Tabs on Super Tuesday</a></p>\u000A<p><a href="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~a/readwriteweb?a=omtx9C"><img src="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~a/readwriteweb?i=omtx9C" border="0" /></a></p><div class="feedflare">\u000A<a href="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~f/readwriteweb?a=S1OsFTE"><img src="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~f/readwriteweb?i=S1OsFTE" border="0" /></a> <a href="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~f/readwriteweb?a=dnZyOeE"><img src="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~f/readwriteweb?i=dnZyOeE" border="0" /></a> <a href="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~f/readwriteweb?a=Gh08Moe"><img src="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~f/readwriteweb?i=Gh08Moe" border="0" /></a> <a href="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~f/readwriteweb?a=BbbnQIe"><img src="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~f/readwriteweb?i=BbbnQIe" border="0" /></a> <a href="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~f/readwriteweb?a=xkOd3te"><img src="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~f/readwriteweb?i=xkOd3te" border="0" /></a> <a href="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~f/readwriteweb?a=sT7nyJE"><img src="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~f/readwriteweb?i=sT7nyJE" border="0" /></a> <a href="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~f/readwriteweb?a=bG52AXE"><img src="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~f/readwriteweb?i=bG52AXE" border="0" /></a>\u000A</div><img src="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/readwriteweb/~4/229682770" height="1" width="1" />

V<p>Five years ago, Tony Blair launched an illegal war of aggression on Iraq.  Now, he <a href="http://politics.guardian.co.uk/eu/story/0,,2251168,00.html">wants to be President of the European Union</a>. VWhy John M\u2019Cain becoming the next America President would be a good thing for New Zealand: Free trade.
p262
sg5
Vhttp://jimmyjangles.blogspot.com/2008/02/why-john-mcain-becoming-next-america.html
p263
sg13
(lp264
sg15
V<p align="left">Mr McCain supports free trade and free trade supports NZ by being its life blood, so any promotion of trade by McCain would likely have benefits for NZ.</p> <p align="left"></p> <p align="left">The following is a fairly rough analysis of the 3 main contenders for the American presidency and their positions on free trade. I assume you believe in free trade and know of its benefits, don't vote green and agree that labour and environmental matters should be left out of trade agreements and pursed by other means. </p>  <p align="left"></p> <p align="left"><strong>John McCain</strong></p> <p align="left"></p> <p align="left">This <a href="http://www.ontheissues.org/John_McCain.htm">site</a> has McCain's position on free trade and it lists (I've edited it and the other lists that follow) his positions as being among:</p> <ul> <p align="left"> <li>Considers subsidies a mistake, and opposes them. </li> <p></p> <p align="left"> <li>Believes very time US went protectionist, America a paid heavy price</li> <p></p> <p align="left"> <li>Supports ethanol, but by exporting, not by subsidies (this might suggest he is against 'infant industry arguments')</li> <p></p> <p align="left"> <li>No environmental provisions in be placed trade agreements. </li> <p></p> <p align="left"> <li>Substitute trade treaties for protectionism. </li> <p></p> <p align="left"> <li>Would admit China to WTO based on their concessions (and keep open trade &amp; diplomacy; but keep eyes open)</li> <p></p> <p align="left"> <li>Free trade with any country except security risks. Retaliatory protectionism is a &quot;murder-suicide pact&quot;. </li> <p></p> <p align="left"> <li>Mexico: balancing act between free trade &amp; stopping drugs. </li> <p></p> <p align="left"> <li>NAFTA has had unambiguously positive impact on US (<a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/North_American_Free_Trade_Agreement">NAFTA</a> -North America Free Trade Agreement. </li> <p></p></p></p></p></p></p></p></p></p></p></ul> <p align="left"></p> <p align="left">The money quote&nbsp; &quot;I don't believe in walls. I believe in freedom. If I were President, I would negotiate a free trade agreement with almost any country willing to negotiate fairly with us. Only risks to the security of our vital interests or egregious offenses to our most cherished political values should disqualify a nation from entering into a free trade agreement with us.&quot;</p>  <p align="left">Thus there is a clear direction that he would take if he became American President. Seeing as he appears to be the front runner for the Republican shot at the Presidency, NZ should be pleased. </p> <p align="left">What of his Democrat opposite? Hilary Clinton and Barack Obama are the two its going to be between.</p><b> <p align="left">Hilary Clinton</p></b> <p align="left">Her position on free trade from the same site:</p> <ul> <p align="left"> <li>Supported NAFTA in 1998; opposed CAFTA since 2005 (<a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/CAFTA">CAFTA </a>- Central America Free Trade Agreement) </li> <li>Export from big agribusiness, but also from small farmers</li> <li>Pro-American trade: NAFTA has hurt workers.</li> <li>No fast-track authority for this president. </li> <li>Better approach: real trade adjustment assistance. </li> <li>End tax breaks for outsourcing jobs. Defended outsourcing of US jobs to India</li> <li>Globalization should not substitute for humanization. </li> <li>Supports MFN for China, despite concerns over human rights. </li></p></ul> <p align="left">The money <a href="http://www.ontheissues.org/2008/Hillary_Clinton_Free_Trade.htm">quote</a> &quot;We've got to have a better approach to trade around the world. And it's important that we have an idea of how to maximize the benefits from the global economy while minimizing the impact on American workers. That includes things like real trade adjustment assistance and other support.&quot;</p>  <p align="left">So kind of a mix bag for the husband of Monica Lewinsky's ex boyfriend. Seems like she wants to be a free trader but probably might be prey to some protectionist ideals. Possibly a Coldplay fan. Her record suggests McCain is a better bet for NZ free trade wise. </p> <b> <p align="left">Barack Omaba</p></b> <p align="left"></p> <p align="left">Barack Omaba is a serious challenger of Clinton. As Oprah said at some rally to vote for him not &quot;because he is black but because he is brilliant'. We'll lets see how brilliant he is at free trade.</p>  <p align="left"></p> <p align="left">Again from the same <a href="http://www.ontheissues.org/Barack_Obama.htm">site </a>that sums the candiates positions up:</p> <ul> <ul> <p align="left"></p></ul> <li>Enforce environmental &amp; labor provisions in trade agreements </li> <li>Enforce existing safety laws against Chinese products </li> <li>NAFTA needs to be amended. </li> <li>Stand firm against CAFTA for labor &amp; environmental standards </li> <li>Congress subsidizes megafarms &amp; hurts family farmers. </li> <li>People don't want cheaper T-shirts if it costs their job. </li> <li>Amend NAFTA to add labor agreements. </li> <li>Reinvest in communities that are burdened by globalization. </li> <li>Insists on labour and human rights standards for China trade. </li> <li>Fair trade should have tangible benefits for US. </li> <li>Voted YES on free trade agreement with Oman. </li> <li>Voted NO on implementing CAFTA for Central America free-trade </li> <ul> <p></p></ul></ul> <p align="left"></p> <p align="left">The money <a href="http://www.ontheissues.org/2008/Barack_Obama_Free_Trade.htm">quote</a> &quot;There's no doubt that NAFTA needs to be amended. I've already said I would contact the president of Mexico and the prime minister of Canada to make sure that labour agreements are enforceable. But I did want to just go back briefly to the issue of trade and human rights that you had mentioned. We have to stand for human rights, and that should be part of the trade equation&quot; </p>  <p align="left"></p> <p align="left">Oh dear, not brilliant at all. I liked the guy before I read this. &nbsp;Appears to be not so inclined to support free trade and very&nbsp;likely to&nbsp;be a little protectionist. Hilary Clinton trounces totally him on.&nbsp;Probably has Coldpay's Rush of Blood to the Head on high rotate at the campaign office. </p>  <p align="left"></p> <p align="left">To conclude it would appear that John M'Cain is greatly more in favour of free trade than Hilary and Obama. If NZ was to pick a player&nbsp;to get benefits for itself&nbsp;- &nbsp;it would have to be him. Should the Democrats win the election, Hilary Clinton would be the better outcome for New Zealand. </p>  <p align="left"></p> <p align="left">As an aside - there are a million reasons why Americans would choose to vote for any of these 3. I think it would be intriguing to see a Black man standing in front of the White house as President. I imagine he would actually try and help people in America. Hilary would just be Hilary \u2013 a lecturer once suggested&nbsp;to me in&nbsp;a tutorial&nbsp;that woman leave their feminity at the door when they enter politics and just follow the behavioural standard set by men - so I don't see her being a woman as significant reason to vote for her in terms of making change&nbsp;\u2013 but maybe that view is tainted by NZ being spoiled by having so many successful women in top jobs and just getting on with it. <font size="2"></font></p> <br /><br /><strong>Update:</strong>  Mr McCain actually <a href="http://wellington.usembassy.gov/senators.html">has been in NZ</a> and totally advocated for the advancement of a FTA with America. I knew this and totally forgot it as I wrote the post - even though it was knowing this that was what inspired it... <br /><br />Rob Good blogged it <a href="http://goodfactor.blogspot.com/2006/01/senator-john-mccain-in-new-zealand.html">here </a>. These chaps had nice things to say <a href="http://www.bilaterals.org/article.php3?id_article=3528">here</a> as did Phil Goff <a href="http://www.beehive.govt.nz/release/senators+mccain+and+sununu+encourage+president+bush+launch+fta+negotiations+new+zealand">here</a><br /><br /><strong>Update 2:</strong> Kiwiblog <a href="http://www.kiwiblog.co.nz/2008/02/well_done_goff.html#comment-404493">notes</a> that a 'US-NZ free trade agreement is now a real possibility with the announcement that the US will begin negotiations with the P4 group of NZ, Brunei, Chile and Singapore'. That's wicked awesome.

VAviary: Flashy Collaborative Media Editing
p281
sg5
Vhttp://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/readwriteweb/~3/229736683/aviary.php
p282
sg13
(lp283
sg15
V<p><img src="http://www.readwriteweb.com/images/aviarylogo.jpg" />Online media processing tool suite <a href="http://a.viary.com">Aviary</a> is opening up two of its many services to those who have requested beta access and a limited number of new requesters.  The first two tools, an image editor and a pattern generator, are impressive and will be followed by a vector editor next month and the rest of the Aviary tools later.</p>\u000A\u000A<p>Photoshop contest site <a href="http://worth1000.com">Worth1000</a> is behind Aviary and built the tools in Flex and Actionscript3.  The primary value of making the image editor social is in allowing users to view multiple steps in an image's creation process.  You can fork off into a new design at any point in the design timeline, you can leave comments, etc.</p>\u000A\u000A<p>Forthcoming tools from Aviary include audio and video editors, a font editor, digital content marketplace service and more.  If you'd like an invite to Aviary's services, just visit the site and the first 100 RWW readers will get in right away.</p>\u000A\u000A<p>The following is a short video demonstrating the image editor made by its creators. Let's be generous and presume that the choice to demonstrate the tool in transforming a young sex object, driven to psychiatric institutionalization into an old, poor, sickly looking image of womanhood reflects only a lack of maturity on the part of the Aviary staff and is not instead a reflection on the quality of their souls.  In other words, <em>leave Britney alone,</em> dudes.  Just another day in the male dominated tech world - may the creatives of the future be more creative than this.</p>\u000A\u000A<p>Either way, it's a good looking set of tools that I look forward to seeing how our readers put to use.<br />\u000A<center><br />\u000A     </center></p>\u000A<p><a href="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~a/readwriteweb?a=g298MT"><img src="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~a/readwriteweb?i=g298MT" border="0" /></a></p><div class="feedflare">\u000A<a href="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~f/readwriteweb?a=P7GsRZE"><img src="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~f/readwriteweb?i=P7GsRZE" border="0" /></a> <a href="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~f/readwriteweb?a=RqabHrE"><img src="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~f/readwriteweb?i=RqabHrE" border="0" /></a> <a href="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~f/readwriteweb?a=7hLuQze"><img src="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~f/readwriteweb?i=7hLuQze" border="0" /></a> <a href="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~f/readwriteweb?a=ZHL3gte"><img src="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~f/readwriteweb?i=ZHL3gte" border="0" /></a> <a href="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~f/readwriteweb?a=xYm1HEe"><img src="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~f/readwriteweb?i=xYm1HEe" border="0" /></a> <a href="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~f/readwriteweb?a=UziyD0E"><img src="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~f/readwriteweb?i=UziyD0E" border="0" /></a> <a href="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~f/readwriteweb?a=xPrRX9E"><img src="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~f/readwriteweb?i=xPrRX9E" border="0" /></a>\u000A</div><img src="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/readwriteweb/~4/229736683" height="1" width="1" />

VBeing economical with the truth, or lying through her teeth?
p293
sg5
Vhttp://hot-topic.co.nz/2008/02/05/being-economical-with-the-truth-or-lying-through-her-teeth/
p294
sg13
(lp295
sg15
V<p><a href="http://hot-topic.co.nz/wp-content/uploads/2008/02/homer.jpg"><img src="http://hot-topic.co.nz/wp-content/uploads/2008/02/homer-tm.jpg" width="82" height="100" alt="homer.jpg" class="left" /></a> Politicians are skilled at manipulating facts to convey any impression they desire. It's called spin, and in its worst cases <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Truthiness" target="_top">truthiness</a> - nicely defined by the man who invented the term, Stephen Colbert of The Colbert Report: <span>"We're not talking about truth, we're talking about something that seems like truth\u2014the truth we want to exist."</span> Out in wingnut land, they want to believe that global warming is not real. So Muriel Newman at her NZ Centre for Political Research <a href="http://www.nzcpr.com/" target="_top">web site</a> starts spinning the facts and, in the middle of a <a href="http://www.nzcpr.com/weekly113.htm" target="_top">rambling attempt</a> to justify a recent <a href="http://www.scoop.co.nz/stories/PO0801/S00246.htm" target="_top">climate crank call for a joint Australia-NZ Royal Commission on climate change</a> manages to come out with the&nbsp;following:</p>\u000A<blockquote>\u000A<p><span>Anyone who claims that the science on global warming is settled is wrong. There is now growing evidence that that the earth is not warming but cooling: since the 1970s the glaciers of the Arctic, Greenland, and the Antarctic have been growing, and since 1998 average world temperatures have been falling with 2006 cooler than 2005 and 2007 cooler&nbsp;still.</span></p>\u000A</blockquote>\u000A<p>This may be what Muriel fervently believes, but it is also completely untrue. So untrue, in fact, that saying it in an attempt to influence public policy amounts to lying. Sadly, in the <a href="http://www.nzcpr.com/forum/viewtopic.php?t=352" target="_top">echo chamber</a> of truthiness around her web site, she gets taken at face value. Out in the wider world, it simply leaves her credibility in&nbsp;tatters.</p>\u000A<p> <a href="http://hot-topic.co.nz/2008/02/05/being-economical-with-the-truth-or-lying-through-her-teeth/#more-316">(more...)</a></p>

VmiVitals Takes Aim at Tough Online Health Market
p305
sg5
Vhttp://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/readwriteweb/~3/229325538/mivitals_online_health.php
p306
sg13
(lp307
sg15
V<p><img src="http://www.readwriteweb.com/images/mivitals_logo.png" /><a href="http://www.mivitals.com/">miVitals</a> is a new Australian startup that has an ambitious goal: to enable individuals to manage their personal health data via a  web application. miVitals describes itself as &quot;a secure online storage system for health and lifestyle records&quot;. The company says that &quot;most people have about 5 professionals involved in their health management: GP, dentist, optician, specialist, pharmacist.&quot; So miVitals aims to be a central repository of a person's health data - and in future to enable them to share relevant pieces with health professionals and family.  </p>\u000A\u000A<p>Probably the main point is that miVitals wants to give consumers <strong>control over their own health data</strong>. If that theme sounds familiar, it's because <a href="http://www.readwriteweb.com/archives/openid_20_finally_launched.php">OpenID</a> and <a href="http://www.readwriteweb.com/archives/most_promising_web_2008_open_source.php">similar initiatives</a> aim to do the same thing for your social networking and other identity data on the Web. Control of one's data is a key driver for many new web apps today.</p>\u000A\u000A<p><img src="http://www.readwriteweb.com/images/rww_files_health2.jpg" align="right" /><em><strong>Note:</strong> this post is the start of a special investigation series into Web-enabled healthcare, sometimes referred to as 'health 2.0'. Over the next few weeks ReadWriteWeb will be looking at recent examples of healthcare web apps and the general trend of utilizing the Internet in the healthcare industry. If you have a healthcare app that you'd like us to take a look at, please email <a href="mailto:tips@readwriteweb.com">tips@readwriteweb.com</a> and include the word 'health' in the subject line.</em></p>\u000A\u000A<h2>miVitals Target Audience</h2>\u000A<p>miVitals is targeting a global audience, including Australia, USA, Canada and the UK. The core health module is available for free, but the company plans to introduce premium services in the future. </p>\u000A<p>As mentioned above, it's a consumer app - and at this stage isn't integrated into healthcare systems. More on that below, but we should note that miVitals isn't claiming to <em>replace</em> medical records. Instead it provides users with &quot;a place for complete history of relevant health information, in much the same way people currently manage their own financial information.&quot; An example given is of a healthy thirty year old professional whose occupation requires extensive international travel. This person, named Brian, &quot;records his regular exercise and keeps track of his immunisations, doctor\u2019s visits and blood pressure using miVitals.&quot;</p>\u000A<h2>Features</h2>\u000A<p>Currently miVitals offers features such as the ability to store your medical records, manage accounts for your family, record appointments, create  an emergency report. Coming soon are further reports, graphing functionality, mobile phone funcntionality, the all-important ability to share information with  health care professionals, and more. Right now, miVitals seems light in features.</p>\u000A<p><img src="http://www.readwriteweb.com/images/mivitals2b.jpg" /><br />\u000A<em>miVitals UI</em></p>\u000A<p><img src="http://www.readwriteweb.com/images/mivitals1b.jpg" /><br />\u000A<em>Example emergency report</em></p>\u000A\u000A<h2>Issues: Privacy &amp; Integration with Health Systems</h2>\u000A<p>miVitals sounds great in theory, and the current app is functional enough. But of course when it comes to health data there are a couple of key issues to overcome:</p>\u000A<p>1) Ensuring that the data is ultra secure and that all privacy bases are covered; and</p>\u000A<p>2) Getting healthcare professionals to use the system.</p>\u000A<p>miVitals has a <a href="http://www.mivitals.com/index.cfm?page=Privacy">Privacy Policy</a> that goes some way to covering the first issue. You still need to convince consumers that their data is truly safe on the Web - which with very personal data like health, is a tough ask. Even I'm not fully comfortable storing my health data online yet.</p>\u000A<p>But the second issue is probably the biggest - and will require integration with existing healthcare IT systems. I asked miVitals if integration with other health systems is on the cards? A miVitals representative told me that yes, it is &quot;absolutely on the development path for the future, along with professionals access to reports that users generate.&quot;</p>\u000A<p>However, integration is a huge obstacle and one that many startups have tried to solve before, including in the original 'dot com' era. One that springs to mind is Jim Clark's famous <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Healtheon">Healtheon</a> startup - as outlined in Michael Lewis' must-read dot com book <a href="http://www.amazon.com/New-Thing-Silicon-Valley-Story/dp/0393048136">The New New Thing</a>, Clark (the co-founder of Netscape and one of Silicon Valley's enduring folk heroes) set out to revolutionize the healthcare industry in the US via an Internet startup named Healtheon. As <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Healtheon">the Wikipedia notes</a>, Healtheon &quot;developed software that essentially placed their company between physicians, patients, and health care institutions, eliminating unnecessary paperwork and facilitating networking and communication amongst the three.&quot; Although initially unsuccessful, in late 1999 Healtheon merged with the Microsoft-backed <a href="http://www.webmd.com/">WebMD</a> - and  today the combined entity is considered the leading health portal. </p>\u000A<h2>Crowded Market</h2>\u000A<p>One of miVitals' problems is that WebMD already does what miVitals sets out to do. As <a href="http://seekingalpha.com/article/46265-webmd-has-tremendous-growth-ahead">Sramana Mitra pointed out</a> in September, &quot;apart from offering articles and diagnostic tools, [WebMD] allows users to store their health records for easy access as they visit different doctors.&quot; See also Sramana's analysis of <a href="http://sramanamitra.com/2007/08/21/web-30-online-health-part-2/">other online health providers</a>. </p>\u000A<p>Plus don't forget that <a href="http://blogoscoped.com/archive/2007-08-14-n43.html">Google is eyeing up</a> the lucrative online health market too! Google is very well placed to offer a web app that organizes users health data, seeing as organizing the world's information is its core mission.</p>\u000A<h2>Conclusion</h2>\u000A<p>miVitals is an ambitious app, but the <strong>competitive landscape is very tough</strong> - and will only get tougher once Google enters the fray. </p>\u000A<p>Also as of now, miVitals essentially requires individuals to do two key things. Firstly, you must obtain your health data from healthcare providers. This is actually no easy task - I have  trouble getting my doctor's office to send prescriptions to my local chemist, let alone getting the data for my own use! Even if you get the data, you then need to enter it into miVitals. Or if you're lucky, you'll get an electronic version - but once again red tape from the health system will likely prevent that. </p>\u000A<p>In other words, the <strong>lack of integration</strong> with current health systems puts up a big obstacle. This is not a new issue; and it won't be fully solved for years to come. Anyone who has dealt with healthcare systems before (which is most of us) knows how tricky and frustrating it is.</p>\u000A<p>One final issue with miVitals: as a user, you'll need to be <strong>motivated by your circumstances</strong> to enter data into miVitals. While the 30 year old  who travels frequently (noted above) has good reason to have a central repository of his health data, this won't be the case for most people. Take me for example: I travel every few months and I have diabetes. But rather than enter my health data into a new system, I'm more inclined to just put some key paper records into my suitcase every time I travel. Unfortunately, any time that you need to duplicate data entry or enter data into a system when there isn't a compelling reason, it puts an extra barrier on web apps.</p>\u000A<p>miVitals does get a lot of points from me for its initiative and goals. Plus the web app itself is nice and the UI nifty. Overall,  in theory the app is great. But there are a lot of practical issues to overcome, plus some very big players already in the market - or about to enter it.</p>\u000A<p><a href="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~a/readwriteweb?a=qmxkAz"><img src="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~a/readwriteweb?i=qmxkAz" border="0" /></a></p><div class="feedflare">\u000A<a href="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~f/readwriteweb?a=prnllLE"><img src="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~f/readwriteweb?i=prnllLE" border="0" /></a> <a href="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~f/readwriteweb?a=HbzHJ1E"><img src="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~f/readwriteweb?i=HbzHJ1E" border="0" /></a> <a href="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~f/readwriteweb?a=v2Rn9Ue"><img src="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~f/readwriteweb?i=v2Rn9Ue" border="0" /></a> <a href="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~f/readwriteweb?a=yb9Iq3e"><img src="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~f/readwriteweb?i=yb9Iq3e" border="0" /></a> <a href="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~f/readwriteweb?a=6fMebWe"><img src="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~f/readwriteweb?i=6fMebWe" border="0" /></a> <a href="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~f/readwriteweb?a=BpixhZE"><img src="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~f/readwriteweb?i=BpixhZE" border="0" /></a> <a href="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~f/readwriteweb?a=0LSyBVE"><img src="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~f/readwriteweb?i=0LSyBVE" border="0" /></a>\u000A</div><img src="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/readwriteweb/~4/229325538" height="1" width="1" />

V<p>Not PC has a <a href="http://pc.blogspot.com/2008/02/one-law-for-all-day.html#links">lengthy post on the Treaty of Waitangi</a>, and how it is about property rights, not partnership.  Well worth a read, even if you don't agree.</p>\u000A<p><a href="http://jimmyjangles.blogspot.com/2008/02/why-john-mcain-becoming-next-america.html">Jimmy Jangles compares</a> the positions of McCain, Clinton and Obama on free trade.  My summary is McCain is a passionate supporter, Clinton is mildly supportive and fence sitting while Obama is against.  It is a useful reminder that one can like Obama's rhetoric but not like his policy positions. I love the quote from McCain:</p>\u000A<blockquote><p><em>"I don't believe in walls. I believe in freedom. If I were President, I would negotiate a free trade agreement with almost any country willing to negotiate fairly with us. Only risks to the security of our vital interests or egregious offenses to our most cherished political values should disqualify a nation from entering into a free trade agreement with us."</em></p></blockquote>\u000A<p>Poneke <a href="http://poneke.wordpress.com/2008/02/01/civic/">chats to Peter Ellis</a>. This time was no exception. \u201CWhen I started at the Civic in 1987, some parents were so PC that we had to call the girls little women, not little girls,\u201D he said while reminiscing about his former workplace, which was regarded as the trendiest in Christchurch. Wealleans, whose wife worked at the Civic for years, mentioned putting a \u201Cdon\u2019t vote Labour\u201D icon on the <a href="http://www.peterellis.org.nz/">Peter Ellis website</a> to protest at the Government\u2019s lack of action on the case, such an icon likely breaching the Electoral Finance Act. \u201CThat\u2019d be great, Winston,\u201D Ellis said immediately. \u201CYou might find yourself sitting in jail with me having to visit you for a change.\u201D</em></p></blockquote>\u000A<p>And on my suggestion of a blog campaign for a Royal Commission:</p>\u000A<blockquote><p><em>\u201CI can\u2019t even drive a car. Some people just aren\u2019t mechanically minded. I\u2019ve managed to wreck five lawnmowers and a washing machine. Imagine what I would do with a computer. Isn\u2019t a blog like a bog with an \u2018l\u2019 in it? From what I\u2019ve heard, some of these young girls today have blogs they use to flash their bits and pieces on. But yes, I don\u2019t see why not. VWhat NOT to learn from Waitangi Day
p382
sg5
Vhttp://libertyscott.blogspot.com/2008/02/what-not-to-learn-from-waitangi-day.html
p383
sg13
(lp384
sg15
V<div align="justify"><a href="http://pc.blogspot.com/2008/02/one-law-for-all-day.html">PC has written an excellent post</a> on Waitangi Day and what it could be, and being in the \u201Cmother country\u201D of course, I wont have that day off.   However, I can reflect on what it is like to be away from all of the wailing and gnashing of teeth that is around when the usual tribe of tired old collectivists seek to treat people on the basis of \u201Cethnicity\u201D not behaviour.<br />~<br />As PC has said:<br />~<br />What the Treaty did do, for which we can all be thankful, was to bring British law to NZ at a time when British law was actually intended to protect the rights of British citizens, and it promised to extend that protection to all who lived here. For many and often differing reasons, that was what the chieftains signed up to.  To become British citizens, with all the rights and privileges thereof.<br />~<br />Indeed!<br />~<br />And yes, I do know that for some, these rights and privileges were in practice more limited, due to sexism for one, and racism.  I know the 19th century was hardly a period of colourblind government anywhere, but in the realm of colonialism the Treaty was a significant step.    No such rights and privileges for Australian aborigines.<br />~<br />Unfortunately, Waitangi Day perennially becomes the rallying point for those who prefer tribalism and separatism, those who believe in intergenerational blame and guilt, and moreso the idea that you can blame your current life on what happened to your ancestors.  <br />~<br />It is identity politics, the notion that what matters most is not what you do, but what group you \u201Cidentify\u201D with.   Interwoven with this is the belief that people treat you according to that identity, and that statistics can \u201Cprove\u201D unfair treatment if members of an \u201Cidentity\u201D perform \u201Cbelow average\u201D.   You know what I mean, the idea that more Maori are in prison not because they committed crimes, but because \u201Cthe system\u201D was against them.   Those of other identities don\u2019t have this disadvantage because the system was \u201Cdesigned by and for them\u201D.  It denies objective analysis, it denies those who reject identity politics as either part of the problem, or traitors. <br />~<br />The corollary of that is the notion that ones life today is directly attributable to what someone else\u2019s ancestors did generations ago.   To carry the notion that being unhealthy, being poorly educated and committing crimes is because you carry the pain of your forefathers is to be psychologically unhinged.   No one can doubt that one\u2019s inheritance matters, but what is done with it matters too.   In fact far more important that material inheritance is the psychological one.   <br />~<br />Did you have parents who loved you, taught the value of hard work, education, respect and support you as your grew and learnt?   That is far more likely to influence whether you commit crime, get a job, look after yourself and do the same to your children.   Then beyond that is what you do with THAT personal inheritance.   Sadly far too many Maori are being told that they don\u2019t have choices, that it isn\u2019t their parents fault they bashed them up or neglected them, but \u201Csociety\u201D.<br />~<br />Waitangi Day could be a day to celebrate the founding of a nation-state, the opportunities it brings to those who live there, the relative freedom, lack of corruption and rule of law that exists. </div><div align="justify">~   </div><div align="justify">When you see those advancing \u201Ctino rangitiratanga\u201D ask yourself what they mean by that?  Do they mean the individual freedom and private property rights that British law SHOULD have granted them (and all citizens)?  Or do they mean they want more government, government based on race, interventionist government, with more taxes and more control over education, broadcasting, property rights and the economy?   Is it a coincidence that almost all those advocating \u201Ctino rangitiratanga\u201D get inspiration from authoritarian socialists?</div><div align="justify">~</div><div align="justify">So don't think of Waitangi Day by race - race is not an objective way to judge a person and it has no place in any considerations of state.   Waitangi Day should be a day to celebrate the common nationhood of New Zealand.   </div><div align="justify">~</div><div align="justify">Then take the concept of one law for all - colourblind - and ask politicians this year, election year, whether they believe in that and what they'll do about it.   Chances are the two main party leaders wont deliver.</div>
