V<div class="snap_preview"><br /><p>The Treaty of Waitangi is not some abstract notion of little importance to anyone. It is New Zealand\u2019s founding constitutional document, and it affects our lives in various real ways, legally and by the manner in which we conduct our public affairs. Waitangi Day is our country\u2019s national day and it is a day worth celebrating, not something to be slightly ashamed of.</p>\u000A<p>Wellingtonians have the opportunity to mark today by checking out the actual Treaty document. Yes, the very one signed on this day in 1840 by Captain William Hobson, RN and the assembled chiefs of the northern tribes at Waitangi. Not many people seem to know that the Treaty is on permanent display in the Constitution Room at <a href="http://www.archives.govt.nz/exhibitions/permanentexhibitions/treaty.php">Archives NZ</a> in Mulgrave St, Wellington, opposite Aitken St. Archives is open today from 10am to 4pm specially for people to look at the Treaty. Go there.</p>\u000A<p>The Treaty was a product of both missionary and official British desire to ensure Maori were treated substantially better than indigenous Australians were when formal British occupation of their country began 52 years before Waitangi. Though settler honouring of the Treaty only lasted until their demands for land exceeded iwi willingness to sell, much that happened in New Zealand was still far and away better than what happened in Australia, as I wrote in <a href="http://poneke.wordpress.com/2007/12/26/sorry/">my December article</a> on new Australian prime minister Kevin Rudd\u2019s intention finally to say \u201Csorry\u201D to the Aborigines for the shameful way they were treated for the best part of 200 years.</p>\u000A<p>Despite the land grabs that took place here and the suppression of much of Maori culture until about 1970, many good things happened too, especially in comparison with Australia and many other colonised countries, and more has been done to make amends in the past three decades than probably anywhere else.</p>\u000A<p>In 1869, a full 100 years before Australian Aborigines were allowed to vote, the colonial New Zealand Parliament extended the franchise to all Maori men, at a time many settler men remained excluded. Maori had to vote in the four special seats created for them, but the fact they were allowed to vote was an important and enlightened development for the time, 24 years before our pioneering enfranchisement of women. New Zealand never had laws overtly discriminating against Maori or preventing them from taking part in civil and political life. Intermarriage has been common and accepted here since Europeans started arriving, to the extent that most people of Maori ancestry now also have European ancestry. There has always been a general goodwill between the races here, even during times of strain and controversy. Since 1970 there has been a remarkable renaissance of Maori culture, language and participation in the political process. The creation of the Waitangi Tribunal in 1975 led to the continuing, honorable, bipartisan settling of land and other grievances dating back to colonial times, a process Australia has barely begun. Not everyone has been happy with the settlement process. Many Pakeha were at the beginning suspicious and opposed, though that has now much waned. Many Maori still feel it is taking too long. But it is nonetheless taking place.</p>\u000A<p>These are things to reflect on, to celebrate and be proud of today, 168 years after the signing of the Treaty. As John Clarke used to sing in his Fred Dagg days, sometimes we don\u2019t know how lucky we are.</p>\u000A<p><b>Other Waitangi blogging:</b> Stef the Ex-expat has <a href="http://exexpat1.blogspot.com/2008/02/pakeha-language-pricks.html">a thoughtful Waitangi Day essay</a> on Pakeha learning te reo. <a href="http://www.kiwiblog.co.nz/2008/02/clark_blunders_again.html">David Farrar</a> says Helen Clark blundered by staying away from Te Tii Marae, while John Key looked prime ministerial. David makes the hilarious point that only in New Zealand could one see the spectacle of someone like John Key "shaking hands with Tame Iti, who was arrested by the police for allegedly being the leader of a group which aimed, amongst other things, to assassinate John Key." <a href="http://pc.blogspot.com/2008/02/one-law-for-all-day.html">Not PC</a> has an interesting, black-letter-law, Eurocentrist view of the Treaty, which, probably deliberately, misses the point that times change.</p>\u000A<img alt="" border="0" src="http://feeds.wordpress.com/1.0/categories/poneke.wordpress.com/86/" /> <img alt="" border="0" src="http://feeds.wordpress.com/1.0/tags/poneke.wordpress.com/86/" /> <a rel="nofollow" href="http://feeds.wordpress.com/1.0/gocomments/poneke.wordpress.com/86/"><img alt="" border="0" src="http://feeds.wordpress.com/1.0/comments/poneke.wordpress.com/86/" /></a> <a rel="nofollow" href="http://feeds.wordpress.com/1.0/godelicious/poneke.wordpress.com/86/"><img alt="" border="0" src="http://feeds.wordpress.com/1.0/delicious/poneke.wordpress.com/86/" /></a> <a rel="nofollow" href="http://feeds.wordpress.com/1.0/gostumble/poneke.wordpress.com/86/"><img alt="" border="0" src="http://feeds.wordpress.com/1.0/stumble/poneke.wordpress.com/86/" /></a> <a rel="nofollow" href="http://feeds.wordpress.com/1.0/godigg/poneke.wordpress.com/86/"><img alt="" border="0" src="http://feeds.wordpress.com/1.0/digg/poneke.wordpress.com/86/" /></a> <a rel="nofollow" href="http://feeds.wordpress.com/1.0/goreddit/poneke.wordpress.com/86/"><img alt="" border="0" src="http://feeds.wordpress.com/1.0/reddit/poneke.wordpress.com/86/" /></a> <img alt="" border="0" src="http://stats.wordpress.com/b.gif?host=poneke.wordpress.com&blog=2287634&post=86&subd=poneke&ref=&feed=1" /></div>

VAlthough outcomes are rated as 'good', waiting times for health treatment in Sweden are now the longest in Europe. <br /><br /><span>Long waits are a hallmark of government health care anywhere it's employed.  When the perception exists that treatment is free (it is not; Swedes pay more than half their gross income in taxes to support the welfare state), system overuse is inevitable.  People can think of no reason to self-ration care.  They show up in emergency rooms and doctor's offices with conditions for which they wouldn't seek treatment if they paid directly at the time of service, says IBD.</span><br /><br /><a href="http://www.ncpa.org/sub/dpd/index.php?Article_ID=15548">More.</a>

V<img src="http://farm3.static.flickr.com/2163/2244598540_aafde6831e_o.gif" />Although we're hopeful that Hollywood's writers strike is nearly at its end, the \u000Aexperience has led us to discover other entertainment venues. One area where \u000Athere seems to be a lot of development lately is in Internet TV. The latest is a \u000A100% indie Internet TV channel with 24/7 programming, created by Jeff Pulver, \u000AVOIP pioneer and the founder of <a href="http://www.pulver.com/">pulver.com</a>. Each week, <a href="http://www.pulver.tv/">pulverTV</a> creates 12-14 hours of their own \u000Aoriginal programming and the rest is culled from over 40 different producers of \u000Aindependently created Internet TV shows from the web. The TV shows span several \u000Adifferent genres including comedy, drama, sci-fi, anime, health, cooking, \u000Alifestyles, fitness, and business/finance.  \u000A\u000A<p>Until the launch of the 24/7 programming, pulverTV was the home of&nbsp; "<a href="http://www.blogtv.com/Shows/96">The Jeff Pulver Show</a>," a program \u000Awhich Jeff has been hosting since April 2007. This show will continue to be one \u000Aof the featured programs on pulverTV, first airing live (you can catch the next \u000Aone on Wednesday, Feb 6th at 2 PM EST), then being re-broadcast later in the \u000Aprogramming schedule. \u000A</p><p>Along with producers Ariel Schwartz and Andy Lipson and sponsor BlogTV, \u000Athe pulverTV channel was formed. One of their main goals with the service is to provide a \u000Aplatform for the indie creators of Internet TV to get their shows discovered. By \u000Aproviding the technology, production, and distribution information to any of \u000Athose who request it, the platform can be a launch point for currently \u000Aundiscovered talent. Alongside that goal is, pulverTV wants to provide quality \u000A24/7 programming in order to close the gap between TV and "Internet TV." \u000A</p><p>Internet TV producers and creators with an existing program they want to \u000Apublicize or with one they want to create can <a href="mailto:jeffp@pulver.com">contact Jeff</a> via email for more information \u000Aon how to get started.</p><p>Always on Internet TV (that isn't lifecasting) - love the idea! However, the current lineup at pulverTV isn't always the most riveting. Still, the idea is good one, and hopefully the talent will follow.<br /></p><p>&nbsp;</p>\u000A\u000A<p><a href="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~a/readwriteweb?a=xJBezu"><img src="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~a/readwriteweb?i=xJBezu" border="0" /></a></p><div class="feedflare">\u000A<a href="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~f/readwriteweb?a=u7TW6sE"><img src="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~f/readwriteweb?i=u7TW6sE" border="0" /></a> <a href="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~f/readwriteweb?a=qWKKqhE"><img src="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~f/readwriteweb?i=qWKKqhE" border="0" /></a> <a href="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~f/readwriteweb?a=ZkhK2te"><img src="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~f/readwriteweb?i=ZkhK2te" border="0" /></a> <a href="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~f/readwriteweb?a=fBY4aOe"><img src="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~f/readwriteweb?i=fBY4aOe" border="0" /></a> <a href="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~f/readwriteweb?a=YhN6OGe"><img src="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~f/readwriteweb?i=YhN6OGe" border="0" /></a> <a href="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~f/readwriteweb?a=JnuzY5E"><img src="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~f/readwriteweb?i=JnuzY5E" border="0" /></a> <a href="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~f/readwriteweb?a=XFKp4kE"><img src="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~f/readwriteweb?i=XFKp4kE" border="0" /></a>\u000A</div><img src="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/readwriteweb/~4/229682769" height="1" width="1" />

VFrancesca Price WA$TED!\u2019s Eco Expert

V<img src="http://bp2.blogger.com/_HZlxBZQcoGI/R6bSGO8WwkI/AAAAAAAABfo/Y9ukoE764HM/s320/francesca+price.JPG" alt="Francesca Price Wa$ted!" title="Francesca Price Wa$ted!" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5163045027359146562" border="0" />Francesca Price presented the first series of <a href="http://www.nzrealitytv.com/search/label/wa%24ted">WA$TED!</a> in 2007 and writes a weekly column for the Listener about \u201Cgreen\u201D issues. She has also written environmental stories for the <span>Sunday Star Times, The NZ Herald</span> and <span>Next Magazine</span>. She is currently finishing a guide book to greener living in New Zealand.<br /><br />Francesca worked as a TV presenter and journalist at the BBC and wrote for a number of newspapers and magazines. She was a reporter for the BBC\u2019s flagship shows, <span>Watchdog, Food</span> <span>and Drink</span> and <span>Holiday </span>before going on to present a live, half hour consumer show for BBC3.<br /><br />She has also written features for The Guardian, The Times and several British magazines.  At the end of 2005, Francesca returned home to New Zealand with her partner and two young daughters. She wanted her family to embrace a simpler, greener way of life. They have settled in the West Auckland suburb of Titirangi where she proudly grows her own veggies, struggles with the Waitakere weeds and strives to live up to the advice she gives everybody else, saying that she feels that everyone checks to make sure she\u2019s always carrying her green eco shopping bags on trips to the supermarket!<br /><br />WA$TED! returns to TV3 on Tuesday 5th Feb at 8pm. The <a href="http://www.fishpond.co.nz/product_info.php?ref=797&products_id=11497584&affiliate_banner_id=1">accompanying book WA$TED!</a> is in stores now, and is full of ways to reduce your household bills and save our planet. The DVD of the series is being used as an educational resource by over 250 schools around the country.<br /><br /><br /><span><span>Photos: Fumes TV<br /></span></span>\u000A<p><a href="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~a/NewZealandRealityTv?a=jwAzgn"><img src="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~a/NewZealandRealityTv?i=jwAzgn" border="0" /></a></p><div class="feedflare">\u000A<a href="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~f/NewZealandRealityTv?a=QMsRUEE"><img src="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~f/NewZealandRealityTv?i=QMsRUEE" border="0" /></a> <a href="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~f/NewZealandRealityTv?a=8bb04Ue"><img src="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~f/NewZealandRealityTv?i=8bb04Ue" border="0" /></a> <a href="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~f/NewZealandRealityTv?a=HlLhtFe"><img src="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~f/NewZealandRealityTv?i=HlLhtFe" border="0" /></a> <a href="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~f/NewZealandRealityTv?a=HEwI64e"><img src="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~f/NewZealandRealityTv?i=HEwI64e" border="0" /></a>\u000A</div><img src="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/NewZealandRealityTv/~4/228783882" height="1" width="1" />

VVidoop Hires OpenID Foundation Chair Scott Kveton
p448
sg5
Vhttp://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/readwriteweb/~3/229808372/vidoop_kveton.php
p449
sg13
(lp450
sg15
V<p><img src="http://www.readwriteweb.com/images/vidooplogo.jpg" />Tulsa, Oklahoma based authentication service <a href="http://vidoop.com">Vidoop</a> announced today that it has hired <a href="http://kveton.com/blog/">Scott Kveton</a>, Chair of the <a href="http://openid.net/wiki/index.php/OpenID_Foundation">OpenID Foundation</a>, to be the company's VP of Open Platforms and the Director of the company's new West Coast office in Portland, Oregon.  With the move Kveton ends a short run at the heavily funded and very interesting <a href="http://mystrands.com">MyStrands</a> recommendation service, a development that raises some questions about that otherwise strong looking operation.</p>\u000A\u000A<p>The addition of Kveton to its staff should push Vidoop into the public consciousness in a big way, concerning OpenID and open platforms.<br />\u000A</p>\u000A\u000A<p><img src="http://www.readwriteweb.com/images/Picture%2023.png" align="right" hspace="5px" vspace="5px" />Kveton is a force to reckon with and an outspoken advocate for Open Platforms. He was a co-founder of the <a href="http://osuosl.org/">Open Source Lab at OSU</a>, a research facility that's provided hosting for <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Open_Source_Lab">a long list of Open Source projects</a> ranging from Mozilla to the Linux Kernel.  He was also the CEO of <a href="http://janrain.com">JanRain</a>, a leading OpenID vendor, and now chairs the OpenID Foundation.</p>\u000A\u000A<p>For readers interested in learning more about OpenID and related data portability matters, Kveton did <a href="http://itc.conversationsnetwork.org/shows/detail3510.html">an excellent interview on Phil Windley's Technometria last month</a> that will satisfy both the uninitiated and the already involved. </p>\u000A\u000A<h2>The Vidoop Product</h2>\u000AVidoop is a small shop made up largely of former US Navy cryptographers.  They are entirely revenue funded and have a really interesting product.  Though there are any number of advanced security features, here's the basic story.  \u000A\u000A<p>Vidoop asks users to select a handful of topical categories which are then used to populate images in a square of largely random tiled images.  See the example below.  If when creating your account with Vidoop you said you like pictures of dogs, birds and board games - then you and only you would know to pick out the letters embedded in the handful of images in a grid presented at login that happen to contain dogs, birds and board games.    <strong>Some of those images will include advertisements!</strong>  In other words, Vidoop has found a way to monetize OpenID authentication - and they are doing it live with a handful of major corporate customers already.  See the sample below.  It's much easier used than explained, by me at least.  </p>\u000A\u000A<p>It's strangely fascinating and I'm not sure how happy I am about the advertisements sneaking their way into my consciousness as I look closely for puppy pictures.  That said, we here at RWW have puppy pictures hidden inside our ads on site too (look!) so who am I to criticize?</p>\u000A\u000A<p>Readers interested in comparing various OpenID providers should see the <a href="http://spreadopenid.org/provider-comparison/">vendor comparison chart at SpreadOpenID.org</a>.</p>\u000A\u000A<center><img src="http://www.readwriteweb.com/images/vidoopscreen.jpg" /></center>\u000A\u000A<p><br />\u000A</p>\u000A<p><a href="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~a/readwriteweb?a=HnZ42w"><img src="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~a/readwriteweb?i=HnZ42w" border="0" /></a></p><div class="feedflare">\u000A<a href="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~f/readwriteweb?a=XFiu06E"><img src="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~f/readwriteweb?i=XFiu06E" border="0" /></a> <a href="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~f/readwriteweb?a=m4LAumE"><img src="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~f/readwriteweb?i=m4LAumE" border="0" /></a> <a href="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~f/readwriteweb?a=C0RWJfe"><img src="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~f/readwriteweb?i=C0RWJfe" border="0" /></a> <a href="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~f/readwriteweb?a=aeS5Dke"><img src="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~f/readwriteweb?i=aeS5Dke" border="0" /></a> <a href="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~f/readwriteweb?a=WJEncse"><img src="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~f/readwriteweb?i=WJEncse" border="0" /></a> <a href="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~f/readwriteweb?a=CYMo2UE"><img src="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~f/readwriteweb?i=CYMo2UE" border="0" /></a> <a href="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~f/readwriteweb?a=7P0n8wE"><img src="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~f/readwriteweb?i=7P0n8wE" border="0" /></a>\u000A</div><img src="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/readwriteweb/~4/229808372" height="1" width="1" />

VWanted: Real Men

V<div>It's not only New Zealand women who are looking for "real men",  it seems New Zealand <a href="http://www.nzherald.co.nz/section/1/story.cfm?c_id=1&objectid=10490687">schools</a> are as well.<br /><br />Everyone knows that teaching these days is a profession reserved for <span>women, Unionists, sissys and homos</span>.  And I mean that in a respectful way.  After all most of them did spend $30,000 of the taxpayers money on scholarships and interest free student loans completing the lofty academic heights of an Arts degree to then find themselves in front of a class of teenagers where plenty of students are actually smarter than they are.<br /><br /><img alt="The image \u201Chttp://media.apn.co.nz/webcontent/image/jpg/lind1.jpg\u201D cannot be displayed, because it contains errors." src="http://media.apn.co.nz/webcontent/image/jpg/lind1.jpg" /> Real man.  Peter Lind.<br /><br /><br /><br /><img alt="The image \u201Chttp://www.feildingag.school.nz/img/r_menzies.jpg\u201D cannot be displayed, because it contains errors." src="http://www.feildingag.school.nz/img/r_menzies.jpg" /> Real man.  Roger Menzies.<br /><br /><img alt="http://images.tvnz.co.nz/tvnz_images/tvone/programmes/seven_periods_with_mr_gormsby/seven_periods_d.jpg" src="http://images.tvnz.co.nz/tvnz_images/tvone/programmes/seven_periods_with_mr_gormsby/seven_periods_d.jpg" /> Real man.  Mr Gormsby.<br /><br /><img alt="http://www.thebriefingroom.com/archives/NEWbenson0001.jpg" src="http://www.thebriefingroom.com/archives/NEWbenson0001.jpg" /> <span>Real man</span>....<span>PSB.<br /><br /></span><img alt="http://img.scoop.co.nz/stories/images/0702/00f18889ed7e11a4c7f3.jpeg" src="http://img.scoop.co.nz/stories/images/0702/00f18889ed7e11a4c7f3.jpeg" /> <span>Real man.  Trevor Mallard with reptile.</span><br /><br />The study's author Penni Cushman reveals the real issue with New Zealand education at present:<br /><br /><span>"Not all boys or girls are going to relate to a man who's a rugby player, because not all boys play rugby."</span><br /><br />Well they bloody well should.  Every boy should play rugby.<br /><br />I mean you can't be a real man unless you have played Saturday morning rugby and had mud stomped in your hair to react with the liniment and inch long abrasions from the sprigs of another players size 5 boot.<br /><br /><span>One respondent in the study - being published in international journal </span><i>Gender and Education</i><span> - referred to the "limp" handshakes of two male teachers who appeared ineffectual and wussy when interviewing for jobs. In that case, strong females were hired instead.</span><br /><br />Well quite right as well.  A limp handshake is a sign of weakness in even a real profession's list.  Put in front of 30 fatherless brats whose mothers were left abandoned each with 3 children and a dog while their father ran off with Debbie from the fish and chip shop to Surfers to escape child support, and the poor limpo would have no shot.<br /><br />The issue of the scarcity of the white hetero male has not changed since I went to school in the 80's.  A young white male heterosexual teacher was a rare thing.  Kind of like a white male Pharmacist or a white male nurse.  The white male heterosexual teacher was soon thrust into a male rolemodel position he couldn't possibly hold up to and was soon either made Principal (<span>as in the case of my fabulous former maths teacher Roger Menzies (above)</span>) or left for greener pastures or to a small town with the music teacher.  That was usually the issue with the white male heterosexual teacher actually - female teachers on staff would thrust themselves all over him and he had trouble keeping his trousers on.<br /><br />That a teacher is white, brown, gay, old, young, male or female shouldn't matter if they are a good teacher.  Hell, it's not like they are rocket scientists.  They stand up in front of a class, attempt to keep some sort of order and recite the curriculum to students who should be fearful to fail exams.  Yes, teachers are AVERAGE members of society.  We should not expect so much of them.<br /><br />They are responsible for failing academic standards, yes.<br /><br />But teachers are absolutely no replacement for good parenting and absent loser fathers.<br /><br />They simply aren't paid enough to be blamed for those sort of ills of society caused by the very parents who demand far too much from them in relation to their child who in many cases is an uncontrollable shit-box at home, why should they be any more controllable at school?<br /></div>

VCompensating for the father famine
p469
sg5
Vhttp://lindsaymitchell.blogspot.com/2008/02/compensating-for-father-famine.html
p470
sg13
(lp471
sg15
VWhat a mixed up and conflicted society we live in. It seems to boil down to not so much a breakdown between the genders but the different amount of trust and respect individuals feel towards the opposite sex. <br /><br />Twenty eight percent of all families with dependent children are being led by just one parent, predominantly female. This has come about through a combination of changed attitudes and changed government provision. As we cannot possibly know the circumstances of all these families I am inclined to accept that collectively there is culpability on both parts. But the overriding ethos of socialists (and male socialists are just as much a part of this attitude) is that men are nearly always at fault when it comes to domestic difficulties. And so the past forty years has seen an increasingly feminist-influenced state compensating for his shortcomings. <br /><br />Unfortunately there is a tendency for some people to turn into what you repeatedly tell them they are - deadbeat dads. And so, even more recently, it hasn't been enough to just replace fathers - they must also be financially and emotionally punished for their inadequacies.<br /><a href="http://www.nzherald.co.nz/section/1/story.cfm?c_id=1&objectid=10490687"><br />NOW</a> we have schools crying out for male teachers to compensate for the father famine. Yet the expectations these guys have to meet (and suspicion they must endure)  is keeping them well away. Who can blame them?<br /><br />What worries me is those women who don't embrace feminist fascism in their everyday lives, don't do a very good job of opposing it. I understand why. "If you are not with us, you are against us," is the intimidating reception one encounters if you dare to criticise their cherished beliefs and institutions.<br /><br />Some men are no angels. But 90 percent of those I have had anything to do with are not womanising pricks, or control freaks, or 'out-of-tune with their feelings' or bad fathers. That may be my good fortune. But I hope that it is more about expectation. We find what we look for. And if women have a singularly low opinion of men, men will reflect it. Heaven knows how the sons of men-maligners mature into anything but men worthy of malign. Behind every bad man is a mother.<br /><br />Much of the feminist distaste for men, especially amongst the lower socio-economic ranks, has now developed into mutual loathing - except when temporary emotional and physical needs demand a ceasefire. Then babies result. And it becomes the preschool and school and secondary schools job to present the child with a positive male role model. But how is he viewed by the mothers? And what has she already inculcated in her female or male child? Is it ever going to be enough to expose a child to one good male role model she has to share and can only keep for a year?  And if she is very young and inclined to physically express her fondness for her daddy-substitute, he has to keep her at a cool and uncompromising arms length. Is that really enough to compensate for a father?<br /><br />I have a flashback to sitting on the back of my father's easy chair on Sunday afternoons while he watched the rugby, me endlessly combing his ever-thinning hair. He never complained. When I was sick he was very patient and would rub my tummy if I was hanging over the toilet vomiting. When I squashed my pet mouse accidentally, breaking its leg, my father made a splint and brought him back to health. (My ever-practical mother wanted to drown it).<br /><br />It is just too sad that so many kids will never experience a good and loving father. And it is even sadder that the state, which is partly to blame for this tragedy, is now desperate to correct it through the education system. As I said last week about Key and Clark's youth policies, it is too little and too late for many of these children.

VStuck in the past
p476

Vhttp://norightturn.blogspot.com/2008/02/stuck-in-past.html

V<p>Why do we have a shortage of male primary school teachers?  One of the reasons is low pay and status (something which forms a nasty feedback loop around feminised and ghettoised professions).  Another is concerns about being accused of sexual abuse.  But a third is the fact that many of our primary school principals are just <a href="http://www.nzherald.co.nz/section/1/story.cfm?c_id=1&objectid=10490687">plain old bigots</a>:\u000A<blockquote>\u000A<i>Many primary school principals believe male primary teachers should be heterosexual, rugby-playing "real men" if they want to be good role models, new research has found.\u000A\u000A<p>One respondent in the study - being published in international journal Gender and Education - referred to the "limp" handshakes of two male teachers who appeared ineffectual and wussy when interviewing for jobs. In that case, strong females were hired instead.</i>\u000A</blockquote>\u000A\u000ASo, perfectly qualified teachers are not being hired because they do not meet some archaic standard of manliness.  What century are these people living in?\u000A\u000A<p>It makes even less sense when you consider the increasing diversity of New Zealand.  The old cult of rugby, racing and beer no longer holds sway, and as study author Penni Cushman points out, not everyone will relate to a rugby-playing teacher because not everyone plays rugby.  But again, it seems our primary school principals are firmly stuck in the past, and unable to cope with or reflect the modern New Zealand.

VPrimary principals seek more real men

V<a href="http://bp0.blogger.com/_Qy4iftwk5JM/R6dbANUzXjI/AAAAAAAACi8/Kxg_j1NOuSQ/s1600-h/lv18_22.jpg"><img src="http://bp0.blogger.com/_Qy4iftwk5JM/R6dbANUzXjI/AAAAAAAACi8/Kxg_j1NOuSQ/s400/lv18_22.jpg" border="0" alt="" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5163195556938604082" /></a><br /><b>breakfast news comment</b><br /><a href="http://www.nzherald.co.nz/section/1/story.cfm?c_id=1&objectid=10490687">Primary principals seek more real men</a><br /><i>Many primary school principals believe male primary teachers should be heterosexual, rugby-playing "real men" if they want to be good role models, new research has found. One respondent in the study - being published in international journal Gender and Education - referred to the "limp" handshakes of two male teachers who appeared ineffectual and wussy when interviewing for jobs. In that case, strong females were hired instead. The findings come amid repeated calls to raise the proportion of male primary school teachers, which fell from 42 per cent in 1956 to just 18 per cent in 2005. Study author Penni Cushman, a University of Canterbury principal lecturer in health education, said the research showed the extent of homophobia and sexism putting men off careers as primary school teachers.</i><br /><br />Isn\u2019t that weird? We all feel that there should be more male teachers in NZ schools, indeed we see time and time and time again that a lack of positive male role models helps contribute to the aggressively violent behaviour of young men, but I had always simply assumed it was because fewer men were applying to be teachers, partly because of a lack of status for the position now and partly because of society\u2019s suspicion towards men around children \u2013 but I NEVER thought for one second it was homophobic principals who are channalling some bullshit 1950s gender stereotype, but when I think about it, it was always the Principal at any school I was at who was always the uptight conservative prick whom everyone resented, if this type of bigotry is as this report suggests widespread,  no wonder schools aren\u2019t such healthy environments for anyone who doesn\u2019t play rugby.

V<a href="http://bp0.blogger.com/_Qy4iftwk5JM/R6daJNUzXiI/AAAAAAAACi0/w5I85Pgb-Oo/s1600-h/ropati6.jpg"><img src="http://bp0.blogger.com/_Qy4iftwk5JM/R6daJNUzXiI/AAAAAAAACi0/w5I85Pgb-Oo/s400/ropati6.jpg" border="0" alt="" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5163194612045798946" /></a><br /><b>breakfast news comment</b><br /><a href="http://www.nzherald.co.nz/section/1/story.cfm?c_id=1&objectid=10490682">Ropatis back off on suit against accuser</a><br /><i>The Ropati family have ruled out taking a private prosecution against the woman who accused former league star Tea Ropati of raping her. Lawyer John Ropati, who was on his brother's legal team, had indicated a private prosecution was being considered because she had gone unpunished for using a class A drug. V<p>The Hive <a href="http://wellingtonhive.blogspot.com/2008/02/how-will-things-look-in-next-few-hours.html">noted earlier today</a> that I didn't rate the Reuters/Zogby poll, but that they did.  Zogby in 1996 and 2000 was often seen as the most accurate pollster but since then they have many bad calls and considerable controversy.</p>\u000A<p>With that in mind it is worth reviewing their polls for Super Tuesday for the most important state of California.</p>\u000A<p>They said Obama was ahead by 13%. VSuper Dooper Tuesday?

V<div align="justify">I am trying hard to resist the only sensation I get from the US primaries, the only thing I can get passionate about, deceptive though it may be, which is to cheer anything that stops Hillary Clinton become President.</div><div align="justify">~</div><div align="justify">You see, it is visceral, it goes back to the days after <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_presidential_election%2C_1992">Bill Clinton was elected with a minority of the popular vote</a> (forgot that, didn't you?), when Hillary decided she had been "elected" too and Bill appointed her to nationalise US health care.   It goes to her views against free market capitalism, and so much of her election platform which is about tinkering, doing more with the federal government, giving away other people's money here and there, and control.  Beyond that is her sense of entitlement to rule - she WANTS power, power over people, and she believes it is her right, her goal to be the first woman President, as if her sex gives her more entitlement.   Her willingness to play dirty against Barack Obama speaks volumes, and has backfired somewhat.   </div><div align="justify">~</div><div align="justify">While Hillary Clinton is, for anyone who believes in individual freedom, and private property rights, an anathema.  Her current opponent, Barack Obama is no better.   He is a nicer, friendlier and more seductive face of exactly the same politics.    There is no substantive difference between Obama and Clinton, indeed <a href="http://newzeal.blogspot.com/2008/01/obama-file-1-forget-islam-look-at.html">Obama's endorsement by those on the left </a>such as the Kennedys (another clan of "born to be rulers"), Democratic Socialists of America and the Communist Party of the USA (hat tip: <a href="http://newzeal.blogspot.com/">New Zeal</a>) makes him potentially more dangerous.</div><div align="justify">~</div><div align="justify">In addition to that, Obama's charisma is a contrast with Clinton's so-called divisiveness.   Obama doesn't excite conservative USA as much as Clinton does - as <a href="http://www.timesonline.co.uk/tol/comment/columnists/andrew_sullivan/article3294433.ece">Andrew Sullivan in the Sunday Times pointed out</a>:</div><div align="justify">~</div><div align="justify"><em>She has extraordinary negatives. She galvanises the conservative movement in ways no other Democrat can. Against McCain, she and she alone enables the Republicans to forget their deep internal divisions and unite. Nothing \u2013 nothing \u2013 unites them as she does. The money she will raise for the Republicans is close to the amount they can raise for themselves.</em></div><div align="justify"><em>~</em></div><div align="justify">Sullivan believes Democrats should pick Obama.  I believe, as difficult as it is to swallow, that it would be better for the world for them to select Clinton.   Obama is a flake, he can speak well, he can inspire, but the substance behind what he says is absent.   The media's inability to quiz him on this has been shocking.</div><div align="justify">~</div><div align="justify">By contrast we know what Clinton believes in, and fortunately, on foreign policy, she is willing to be braver than Obama.  She is pro-Israel, she supports sanctions against Cuba, she supported a resolution calling Iran's Army of the Guards of National Revolution terrorists,  she voted in favour of authorising military force against Iraq and she stated on CNN that "<em>The first obligation of the president of the United States is to protect and defend the United States of America</em>".   For her many many flaws, I would feel slightly safer with Clinton than Obama.</div><div align="justify">~</div><div align="justify">Oh yes there are Republicans.  Romney the flip flopper, who once was seen with Margaret Thatcher, will not win.    John McCain, who is Republican lite, or a member of the rightwing end of the Democratic Party, will win the nomination.   The best you can hope for with him is that he wont reverse the Bush tax cuts.   woopee.</div><div align="justify"> </div><div align="justify"> </div><div align="justify"> </div><div align="justify"> </div>

V<p><a href="http://www.stuff.co.nz/blogs/wp-content/uploads/2008/02/matt_grins.jpg" title="matt_grins.jpg"></a><img vspace="5" align="right" src="http://www.stuff.co.nz/blogs/wp-content/uploads/2008/02/matt_grins.jpg" hspace="5" alt="matt_grins.jpg" title="matt_grins.jpg" />While not known for his comedy skills (did anyone see <em>Stuck On You</em>? Worst comedy about Siamese twins ever!), Matt Damon was nevertheless voted sexiest man last year.</p>\u000A<p>He's probably best known for his action-man amnesiac spy in the <em>Bourne</em> trilogy of films and for playing the not-as-handsome-as-George-or-Brad sidekick in the <em>Ocean's</em> trilogy, but <a target="_blank" href="http://nz.youtube.com/watch?v=ZWTzyU5MFgM"><strong>he was memorably spoofed in <em>Team America: World Police</em></strong></a> after his puppet turned out looking a bit brain-damaged, and the <em>South Park</em> guys decided to give him a voice to match.</p>\u000A<p>Well, in this startling example of how-not-to-tell-your-famous-TV-host-boyfriend-you're-cheating-on-him, Damon proves he might have a funny bone under that meaty frame. (Also does anyone else think Damon looks surprisingly like Leo DiCaprio when he gets angry? I was impressed by the way his face actually turns red while he's ranting.)</p>\u000A<p>He can be quite amusing on other talk shows too, aside from notoriously dumping his girlfriend Minnie Driver live on Oprah, that is (maybe he was trying to avoid <a target="_blank" href="http://nz.youtube.com/watch?v=Rq0apHW6Ezw"><strong>an intense break-up scene like this one</strong></a>), he also does a mean impersonation of <a target="_blank" href="http://www.imdb.com/name/nm0000190/"><strong>Matthew McConaughey</strong></a> as <a target="_blank" href="http://nz.youtube.com/watch?v=CuYD2cwMbpw&NR=1"><strong>demonstrated here on <em>Letterman</em></strong></a>.</p>

VCIA admits torture
p604
sg5
Vhttp://norightturn.blogspot.com/2008/02/cia-admits-torture.html
p605
sg13
(lp606
sg15
V<p>CIA director Michael Hayden has <a href="http://news.bbc.co.uk/2/hi/americas/7229169.stm">admitted to Congress</a> that the CIA <a href="http://norightturn.blogspot.com/2005/11/what-us-does-to-prisoners.html">waterboarded</a> suspected terrorists.  He made excuses and attempted to justify this unjustifiable act, but the fact remains: the CIA tortured prisoners, in contravention of both <a href="http://www.unhchr.ch/html/menu3/b/h_cat39.htm">international</a> and <a href="http://www4.law.cornell.edu/uscode/html/uscode18/usc_sup_01_18_10_I_20_113C.html">US</a> law. The question now is what Congress is going to do about it.  And if the answer is anything less than commencing a full inquiry with the ultimate goal of putting everyone involved - from the torturers who held these screaming men down and poured water down their throats, to the doctors and psychologists who carefully checked their health and certified that they could be safely tortured, to the bureaucrats and lawyers who developed the policy and the legal excuses, to the politicians who personally approved it for each victim - behind bars for a very long time, then the entire US legislature becomes complicit.

VClark blunders again

V<p>Watching TV3 News last night, it appears clear Clark has blundered again with her boycott of the full Waitangi programme.</p>\u000A<p>John Key didn't just look comfortable at Waitangi - he looked Prime Ministerial, and was almost greeted as such, while Clark was missing in action.</p>\u000A<p>I did enjoy the only in NZ absurdity of Key being greeted by, and shaking hands with, Tame Iti who was arrested by the Police for allegedly being the leader of a group which aimed, amongst other things, to assassinate John Key.  However only once he had actually become PM! Could you imagine this in any other country.</p>\u000A<p>And even more bizarrely the costs of the Iti family going to Waitangi are being <a href="http://www.stuff.co.nz/4388969a10.html">paid for by Television New Zealand</a>.</p>\u000A<p>Colin Espiner <a href="http://www.stuff.co.nz/blogs/politics/2008/02/05/clarks-no-show-at-waitangi-a-political-risk/">blogged yesterday</a> that Clark no-show was a risk</p>\u000A<blockquote><p><em>Key, too, is on to a winner whatever happens. While National leaders have not always been welcome at Te Tii, Key is so easy-going and charming that he is unlikely to cop a faceful of mud like his predecessor. But even if he was abused, it simply plays into his favour. It shows that he\u2019s prepared to face up to criticism, while his counterpart is not.</em></p>\u000A<p><em>... Being the Prime Minister is a little different, of course. One does have to keep one\u2019s dignity. But I wonder whether this would have been the year to take the risk and return to Te Tii.</em></p></blockquote>\u000A<p>Audrey Young <a href="http://www.nzherald.co.nz/blog/story.cfm?c_id=1501219&objectid=10490792&ref=rss">also blogged</a> about Key at Waitangi:</p>\u000A<blockquote><p><em>It has been John Key's Waitangi so far today, not Helen Clark's who is just about to land in the Far North.</em></p></blockquote>\u000A<p>And the bizarre spectacle of the PM who refuses to turn up, <a href="http://www.nzherald.co.nz/section/1/story.cfm?c_id=1&objectid=10490884">criticising the warm reception John Key received</a>. She just sounds bitter and small. And her lack of judgement comes through even more when she suggests that Key is not being honest about his agenda - because in fact the media have been reporting that Key has not been delivering a different message to a different audience, and despite the unpopularity has confirmed National policy is still to abolish the Maori seats and not abolish the Foreshore &amp; Seabed Act.</p>\u000A<p>Finally on radio this morning, I <a href="http://www.newstalkzb.co.nz/newsdetail1.asp?storyID=131834">hear that John Key was asked to lead a prayer</a> of his own at the dawn service, as the PM wasn't there. Again this just makes him look like he is the PM, not just wanting to be.  Clark has surrendered her most important weapon - incumbency.</p>\u000A<p>The result of the next election is by no means already determined.  But Labour needs a error-free year, and so far there have been two blunders barely one month in.</p>

VBooks You Should Be Reading Number 40 Of A Bunch
p643
sg5
Vhttp://brainstab.blogspot.com/2008/02/books-you-should-be-reading-number-40.html
p644
sg13
(lp645
sg15
V<a href="http://coppersblog.blogspot.com/">Wasting Police Time by PC David Copperfield</a><br /><br />The most predictable thing about being involved in violent incidents is that they are completely unpredictable. <br />If I respond to a report of thirty youths fighting in the street with baseball bats, I can be fairly certain that on my arrival they will have dispersed and that a subsequent area search will prove negative.<br />On the other hand, if the local library assistant rings up to report a problem customer returning a book late, you just know that you\u2019re going to end up rolling around on the floor somewhere between Late Medieval History and Local Walks.<br /><br />...<br /><br />This book is an edited and tidied up version of coppersblog (see above link), which is just what it sounds like. The pseudonymous David Copperfield is a bit older than me, but out-curmudgeons me and makes it look easy: he is an old fashioned conservative, who believes the main problem with the justice system is that the prisons insist on releasing people after set lengths of time, instead of throwing away the key and letting them rot. Of course, given that my one major swing to the right is on the issue of crime, I pretty much agree with him. (That having been said; he does suffer from that particular myopia common to the middle classes of a certain age, of seeing crime committed by the young and/or poor as more serious than, you know, \u201Csmall\u201D crime; for example, he thinks that drunk and disorderly behaviour - more often than not committed by young morons - should be punished not with community service or periodic detention, rather with a jail sentence of no less than a year, but he also thinks that the punishment for drunk driving \u2013 essentially demerit points \u2013 is overly harsh on people who need their cars to go to work or to ferry their kids around...)<br /><br />Wasting Police Time has a bunch of opinions I don\u2019t agree with (cocooning those few that I do), but is a funny read, and does highlight many problems with policing in England \u2013 in fact, after the first edition of the book was released, questions were raised in Parliament by Opposition MPs who mentioned the book by name. And if nothing else, it possesses the following piece of wisdom:<br /><i>Drugs are fun and they make you feel good, and that\u2019s the extent of it. They do not \u2018cause\u2019 crime, though, any more than the existence of DVD players causes burglary, or the existence of short, ginger children causes bullying.</i>

VFacebook Graduates: Now Do Something For the World
p682
sg5
Vhttp://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/readwriteweb/~3/229914302/facebook_social_change.php
p683
sg13
(lp684
sg15
V<p><img border="0" src="http://www.readwriteweb.com/images/facebook-logo.jpg" width="100" height="35" />Yesterday marked <a href="http://www.facebook.com/">Facebook</a>'s four year anniversary, or to look at it from the college perspective to which the site owes its success: Facebook graduated.  Washington Post assistant editor Rachel Dry, who was a senior at Harvard when Mark Zuckerberg launched thefacebook.com from his college dorm room on February 4, 2004, wrote a <a href="http://www.tnr.com/politics/story.html?id=feb72ee5-35c2-4896-8f4d-53100fad177c">commencement address</a> for <i>The New Republic</i>.  In it, Dry wonders if Facebook is taking "on the big inequities," as Bill Gates -- like Zuckerberg, a famous Harvard dropout -- urged in his commencement speech at the university last year.  We wondered the same thing.</p>\u000A\u000A<p>Last week, we wrote about how <a href="http://www.twitter.com/">Twitter</a>, our <a href="http://www.readwriteweb.com/archives/best_web_littleco_of_2007_twitter.php">Best Web LittleCo</a> of 2007, was quickly morphing into a <a href="http://www.readwriteweb.com/archives/the_rise_of_twitter_as_a_platform_for_serious_discourse.php">viable platform for serious discussion</a>.  One can see that happening today, as Super Tuesday primary elections take place across the US and people report and debate the results across Twitter.  But what about Facebook?  It was, afterall, our <a href="http://www.readwriteweb.com/archives/best_web_bigco_of_2007.php">Best Web BigCo</a> of last year, one that we called a "company that really came of age this year; and [...] was the catalyst for some important Web trends."</p>\u000A\u000A<p>So we started wondering, could Facebook be a catalyst for something else: social change.  Dry mentions the <a href="http://www.facebook.com/apps/application.php?id=2318966938">Causes</a> application on Facebook, and groups which "connect thousands of people with common interests in humanitarian efforts."  Dry also talks about Facebook as an organizational tool, writing, "it's very easy for people to organize races for cures and alert their 547 nearest and dearest to articles on under-covered international tragedies."</p>\u000A\u000A<h2>Facebook as a Vehicle for Social Change</h2>\u000A\u000A<p>Indeed, on Facebook's graduation day a massive political protest in Colombia demonstrated Facebook's power to rally people to a cause.  Monday afternoon hundreds of thousands of Colombians took to the streets to protest the Marxist rebel group <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Revolutionary_Armed_Forces_of_Colombia">FARC</a>.  Estimates on the crowd size ranged from <a href="http://news.bbc.co.uk/2/hi/americas/7225824.stm">500,000 to 2 million</a> people, which in and of itself isn't all that extraordinary -- millions of people get together to protest things all the time.  What is extraordinary, is that the protest was organized largely online through Facebook.</p>\u000A\u000A<p>A Facebook <a href="http://www.facebook.com/event.php?eid=7284103926">event page</a> created by protest organizers attracted over 106,000 confirmed guests with 18,000 maybes.  Almost 320,000 people were invited to the event, which demonstrates the ability for Facebook to get the word out to a massive number of people about social and political issues, quickly and effectively.</p>\u000A\u000A<p>Another example of someone successfully using Facebook to enact change is the "<a href="http://www.facebook.com/group.php?gid=2209409131">For Every 1,000 that join this group I will donate $1 for Darfur</a>," which was started by NYU student Marek Grodzicki.  The group has 424,000 members -- or $424 -- and Grodzicki is renewing his pledge for next year.  That may not be a lot of money, but it's almost half a million people who may now be more aware of an issue because a single person was able to reach them simply by announcing an altruistic act on Facebook and letting viral nature of social networking take over.</p>\u000A\u000A<p>But how common are examples like the FARC protest and the Darfur donation group?  It's really hard to tell, but what we can look at, is the effectiveness of the previously mentioned Causes application to raise money.  Just how charitable are Facebook users?  It turns out... not very.  Or at least, Facebook isn't prompting people to be charitable -- they may give plenty via other channels.</p>\u000A\u000A<p>The Causes app, which allows anyone to create a cause and link it to a registered non-profit organization in the US or Canada, is one of the most popular on Facebook with 10.8 million registered users.  Because Causes interfaces with <a href="http://www.networkforgood.org/">Network for Good</a>, users can set up donation pages for thousands of charities, making it difficult to figure out how successful the application is as a whole.  However, looking at the top five campaigns by users, the results aren't so promising in terms of money raised:</p>\u000A\u000A<p>\u000A<table border="1" cellspacing="0" cellpadding="2" width="600">\u000A<tbody>\u000A<tr>\u000A\u000A<td width="133" valign="top"><strong>Cause</strong></td>\u000A<td width="133" valign="top"><strong>Users</strong></td>\u000A<td width="133" valign="top"><strong>Donations</strong></td>\u000A<td width="133" valign="top"><strong>Per User</strong></td>\u000A</tr>\u000A\u000A<tr>\u000A<td width="133" valign="top">Cancer Research</td>\u000A<td width="133" valign="top">3,005,750</td>\u000A<td width="133" valign="top">$58,520</td>\u000A<td width="133" valign="top">$0.02</td>\u000A</tr>\u000A\u000A<tr>\u000A<td width="133" valign="top">Stop Global Warming</td>\u000A<td width="133" valign="top">1,681,907</td>\u000A<td width="133" valign="top">$20,908</td>\u000A<td width="133" valign="top">$0.01</td>\u000A</tr>\u000A\u000A<tr>\u000A<td width="133" valign="top">Animal Rights</td>\u000A<td width="133" valign="top">1,232,162</td>\u000A<td width="133" valign="top">$19,423</td>\u000A<td width="133" valign="top">$0.02</td>\u000A</tr>\u000A\u000A<tr>\u000A<td width="133" valign="top">Against Child Abuse</td>\u000A<td width="133" valign="top">927,120</td>\u000A<td width="133" valign="top">$7,685</td>\u000A<td width="133" valign="top">$0.01</td>\u000A</tr>\u000A\u000A<tr>\u000A<td width="133" valign="top">Save Darfur</td>\u000A<td width="133" valign="top">800,674</td>\u000A<td width="133" valign="top">$12,528</td>\u000A<td width="133" valign="top">$0.02</td>\u000A</tr>\u000A\u000A</tbody>\u000A</table>\u000A</p>\u000A\u000A<p>Clearly, these are important issues that a lot of people care about, but the application isn't doing much to inspire people to donate money to the causes.  An average of 1 to 2 cents per user isn't really anything to write home about.</p>\u000A\u000A<p>Recently, the Causes app held a contest in which it gave out a $50,000 top prize to the organization that collected the most donations over a six week span.  That's a great idea because even organizations that don't land the $50,000 prize theoretically see an increase in donations.  The Giving Challenge began on December 14th and ended on February 1st, and though the official results won't be announced until later in the month, unofficial results predict the "Love Without Boundaries Foundation" as the winner of the top prize with 4,564 donors.  The participants in the Giving Challenge, who were mostly smaller charities, have much higher per user giving rates than the larger causes -- "Love Without Boundaries," for example, has a per user average over $15.</p>\u000A\u000A<p>But even while the challenge made the Causes app a successful fundraising tool for a handful of small charities, it also exposed the same sort of apathy (at least when it comes to giving) that the top causes seem to deal with.  As part of the competition, Causes gave out a daily $1,000 prize to the charity that had the most donors each day.  Except for the final week, when a couple of charities were making a big push for the top prize, the daily winner generally had under 100 donors.  That may seem like a lot, but with over 30 million people in the US and Canada over the age of 16, it still feels somewhat underwhelming.</p>\u000A\u000A<p>However, even if Causes isn't doing much to raise money, it is potentially doing a lot to raise awareness.  When just the top 5 causes reach about 7.5 million people, that's pretty powerful stuff. Further, each cause is given a group page that has familiar Facebook tools like a wall -- the Cancer Research cause, for example, has nearly 8,000 wall posts.  Giving 3 million people a platform to discuss something they're passionate about and raise awareness -- whether or not it leads to money donated -- points to Facebook's potential as a powerful social tool.</p>\u000A\u000A<p>The bad news for Causes is that like other applications on Facebook, it has recently appeared susceptible to <a href="http://www.readwriteweb.com/archives/have_facebook_apps_peaked_in_popularity.php">app fatigue</a>.  It still has a huge installed based, but its active user base has been sliced to about 1/4th of what it was just a few months ago.</p>\u000A\u000A<h2>Conclusion</h2>\u000A\u000A<p>So is Facebook really a viable platform for social change?  I think it can be.  But like any new platform, we're still learning how to use it most successfully.  There have been some major successes -- like the FARC protest and the participants in the Causes Giving Challenge -- but also some less than stellar performances.</p>\u000A\u000A<p>Facebook still has some growing up to do.  But as the user base gets older and more comfortable with the site, and as developers and organizers figure out the best ways to exploit Facebook to precipitate social change, it certainly could become a very important tool in any organizer's arsenal.</p>\u000A\u000A<p>What do you think?  Can Facebook be a serious platform for eliciting social change?  Or will it never be more than a place to play Scrabulous and poke friends?  Can it ever work for real fundraising?  Share your thoughts in the comments below.</p>\u000A<p><a href="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~a/readwriteweb?a=TjPBAi"><img src="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~a/readwriteweb?i=TjPBAi" border="0" /></a></p><div class="feedflare">\u000A<a href="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~f/readwriteweb?a=PU6rTZE"><img src="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~f/readwriteweb?i=PU6rTZE" border="0" /></a> <a href="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~f/readwriteweb?a=Z4lQQqE"><img src="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~f/readwriteweb?i=Z4lQQqE" border="0" /></a> <a href="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~f/readwriteweb?a=e7Lo7Be"><img src="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~f/readwriteweb?i=e7Lo7Be" border="0" /></a> <a href="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~f/readwriteweb?a=3X5N3ge"><img src="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~f/readwriteweb?i=3X5N3ge" border="0" /></a> <a href="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~f/readwriteweb?a=krM8ySe"><img src="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~f/readwriteweb?i=krM8ySe" border="0" /></a> <a href="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~f/readwriteweb?a=0hBUnsE"><img src="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~f/readwriteweb?i=0hBUnsE" border="0" /></a> <a href="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~f/readwriteweb?a=C8d2umE"><img src="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~f/readwriteweb?i=C8d2umE" border="0" /></a>\u000A</div><img src="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/readwriteweb/~4/229914302" height="1" width="1" />

VSuper-duper Tuesday

p755

V<p>It's <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Super_Tuesday_%282008%29">super-duper Tuesday</a> (can they please get a better name than that?), the day on which most delegates in the US primaries are distributed.  By ths time tomorrow, there'll probably be a Republican nominee (thus effectively disenfranchising all the states which come after); thanks to the Democrats' embrace of proportional representation (or at least proportional distribution of delegates), they're unlikely to have an obvious winner, but the picture may become clearer.  No doubt they'll then have an attack of angst about how a robust contest to be the nominee is a sign of weakness and disunity or something - yet another problem with the US's ludicrous primary system.  Of course, if they had their primaries all at the same time, then it simply wouldn't be a problem.\u000A\u000A<p>For those who are interested, the BBC has an interactive guide to super-duper Tuesday <a href="http://news.bbc.co.uk/2/hi/in_depth/629/629/7223461.stm">here</a>.

VObama-file 9 US Communists Explain  Backing For Barack Obama
p821
sg5
Vhttp://newzeal.blogspot.com/2008/02/obama-file-9-us-communists-explain.html
p822
sg13
(lp823
sg15
VObama-file 8 <a href="http://newzeal.blogspot.com/2008/01/obama-file-8-baltimore-communists-back.html">here</a><br /><br />The Communist Party USA has abandoned it's pretense of neutrality . <br /><br />It is throwing all its energies behind Barack Obama in the race for the Deomocratic Party presidential nomination.<br /><br />Why?<br /><br />I'll let three top US Communists explain;<br /><br />According to <a href="http://paeditorsblog.blogspot.com/2008/01/will-progressives-respond.html">Terrie Albano</a>, editor of the CPUSA's People's Weekly World; <br /><br /><a href="http://bp3.blogger.com/_JtTfGekhAhY/R6LsGy_In5I/AAAAAAAABUk/HDqC8Z4NW7o/s1600-h/1551-150x150.jpg"><img src="http://bp3.blogger.com/_JtTfGekhAhY/R6LsGy_In5I/AAAAAAAABUk/HDqC8Z4NW7o/s200/1551-150x150.jpg" border="0" alt="" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5161947724429959058" /></a><br /><em>The movement that has exploded around Obama is so important. It's antiracist in essence. It's deep and broad and multiracial and multigenerational. It has insightful and sophisticated everyday people active in it. It's the cream rising to the top after the long horrendous period of the Bush administration and ultra right rule since Reagan.<br /><br />But even if Obama doesn't win and Hillary Clinton does, getting rid of any ultra rightist will take this country forward. And the movement around Obama will influence Clinton.<br /><br />This kind of upsurge comes around just once in a lifetime. I hope for all progressives - each of us - get involved. Don't stand on the sidelines. Be active. Don't let history pass you by.</em><br /><br />Pepe Lozano is a leader of the Chicago Young Communist League and is a People\u2019s Weekly World editorial board member.<br /><br /><a href="http://bp0.blogger.com/_JtTfGekhAhY/R6LtvC_In7I/AAAAAAAABU0/9obseloYx5s/s1600-h/m_471edfd9347a242e3ed43f8cd6de0ce6.jpg"><img src="http://bp0.blogger.com/_JtTfGekhAhY/R6LtvC_In7I/AAAAAAAABU0/9obseloYx5s/s200/m_471edfd9347a242e3ed43f8cd6de0ce6.jpg" border="0" alt="" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5161949515431321522" /></a><br />Pepe Lozano's late father, Rudy Lozano, was a leading Chicago activist until his murder in 1983. Shortly before Lozano's death, newly elected Chicago Mayor, Harold Washington enlisted him as his liaison to the Latino community.<br /><br />Rudy Lozano played a big role in building the white "<em>progressive</em>"/Black/Latino coalition that elected Washington, the first black mayor of a major US city.<br /><br />This coalition was <a href="http://newzeal.blogspot.com/2007/10/chicagos-redblack-alliance-targets.html">organised by the CPUSA </a>and Chicago's socialist community that would later coalesce into the Chicago branch of the <a href="http://newzeal.blogspot.com/2008/01/obama-file-2-barack-obama-was-endorsed.html">Democratic Socialists of America</a>.<br /><br />Washington was a <a href="http://newzeal.blogspot.com/2008/01/obama-file-7-barack-obama-and.html">longtime supporter </a>of both groups and a probable secret member of the CPUSA. On taking office he proceeded to stack City Hall with communists, socialists and "<em>progressives</em>."<br /><br />This socialist "<em>golden age</em>" ended with Washington's death in office in 1987, but the alliance that elected him went on to elect <a href="http://newzeal.blogspot.com/2007/12/carol-moseley-braun-did-clinton-send-as.html">Carol Moseley Braun </a>to the US Senate in 1992.<br /><br />It has also supported Barack Obama at least since his successful State Senate race in 1996.<br /><br />According to Pepe Lozano;<br /><br /><em>African Americans and Mexican Americans \u2014 and really all Latinos \u2014 have much to gain in the 2008 elections. There are opportunities for both communities to work together and lead the growing movement for political change in Washington. <br /><br />The Black-Latino alliance is a major force that brings our communities closer in a world where racism, economic injustice and inequalities are deeply rooted throughout every aspect of our past and present. <br /><br />One example of how such unity brought progress for everyone was the campaign to elect Harold Washington mayor of Chicago...  <br /><br />Washington made history that year and put Chicago on the map due to the coalition of Black, Latino and white progressive forces that culminated in a record turnout of voters...<br /><br />The multiracial coalition for political unity that put Washington in office was in large part due to the Latino vote, which by itself had a record turnout of 62 percent, 82 percent of whom voted for Washington. <br /><br />Like Harold Washington, Sen. Barack Obama, on a much larger scale, could make political history by becoming the first African American president. And if it wasn\u2019t for Washington\u2019s example and the coalition forces in Chicago at that time, Obama might not be in the position he is in today.</em> <br /><br />While modern Latino's lean heavily towards Hillary Clinton, Lozano believes they can and should be turned Obama's way.<br /><br /><em>There have been some talk that Mexican Americans and other Latinos aren\u2019t going to vote for Obama, that we \u201Caren\u2019t ready\u201D to vote for a Black man or we have nothing in common. <br /><br />It is false to assume that Latinos are not prepared to vote for Obama. Or by extension that Latinos and Blacks have nothing in common. <br /><br />Latinos of all nationalities, U.S. born or immigrant, men and women, younger and older, have to be agents of change too and reach out to others. That\u2019s what was done during the historic Washington election \u2014 and the whole city won with that victory. <br /><br />In order to do that we must continue to fight for multiracial unity, and the African American and Latino communities together have to be in the forefront pushing a pro-people agenda. <br /><br />So let the reactionaries tremble at our unity in action. Together we have nothing to lose but our common oppression. And we have an election to win! </em><br /><br />Contributing editor to the CPUSA's Political Affairs, <a href="http://paeditorsblog.blogspot.com/2008/01/edwards-withdraws-some-thoughts-about.html">Norman Markowitz</a>, hopes that Obama will change the course of US politics.<br /><br /><a href="http://bp3.blogger.com/_JtTfGekhAhY/R6Lsgy_In6I/AAAAAAAABUs/zGJT0EU3isM/s1600-h/1929-275x275.jpg"><img src="http://bp3.blogger.com/_JtTfGekhAhY/R6Lsgy_In6I/AAAAAAAABUs/zGJT0EU3isM/s200/1929-275x275.jpg" border="0" alt="" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5161948171106557858" /></a><br /><em>Progressives seeking to build a national majority coalition that would both end and dismantle nearly thirty years of right-wing political power in the United States suffered a setback (that is all, I think, it can be called) with the apparent announcement that John Edwards is withdrawing his candidacy. <br /><br />Some, myself included, had hoped that Edwards would stay in, continue to win delegates, and form a coalition with Senator Obama's delegates at the convention to develop both a program and a presidential slate that would decisively defeat the right-wing Republicans and begin to enact in the 21st century programs like national public health care, substantial increases in minimum wages and other labor and social programs, funded through progressive taxation...</em><br /><br />Markowitz believes that Obama will repeat the 1930's. At that time the CPUSA flooded into Franklin Roosevelt's "<em>New Deal</em>" and pushed the USA far to the left.<br /><br /><em>Senator Obama has attracted people of progressive views, many of whom have been alienated from politics or are having their first experience with political activities, in a way that few candidates have for a very long time...<br /><br />He is far less of a known commodity, far more likely to bring into government independents and progressives from the mass organizations and the communities along with the traditional Democratic organization politicians, as Franklin Roosevelt did during the depression... <br /><br />But he can, I think, turn his status as an African American, a member of the minority group most stigmatized in U.S. history, into a very positive force, becoming in effect a real unifying leader for working class and progressive people of all colors, ethnicities and sexual orientations... <br /><br />All of these conjectures may be meaningless if Clinton wins a large victory in next week's "Super Tuesday," which is a good reason for progressives to both vote for and get out the vote for Obama...</em><br /><br />Obama-file 10 <a href="http://newzeal.blogspot.com/2008/02/obama-file-10-barack-obama-and.html">here</a>

V<p>I'm just heading out for 90 minutes or so for a walk with Accident Girl and her dogs.  I expect some results to start to flow through soon, so use this thread for updates.</p>\u000A<p><a href="http://www.politico.com/news/stories/0208/8338.html">Huckabee has beaten Romney in West Virginia</a>, which was unexpected.  McCain supporters may have voted tactically.</p>\u000A<p>The <a href="http://www.pollster.com/blogs/somebodys_gonna_be_wrong.php">polls in California</a> range from Clinton ahead by 10% to Obama ahead by 13%.</p>\u000A<p>It also looks very <a href="http://www.realclearpolitics.com/epolls/2008/president/ca/california_republican_primary-258.html">close for McCain and Romney in California</a>.  Most other places look good for McCain though.</p>\u000A<p>UPDATE: Back now.  For results below I will show after each state the number of delegates up for grabs for Democrats and then Republican, and then the results.  Remember many Republican contests are winner take all, but no Democrats are.</p>\u000A<p>Georgia (103/72): Obama by 23%, Huckabee over McCain by <strike>2</strike>3% so not call yet</p>\u000A<p>Tennessee (68/39): Clinton by <strike>18</strike>28%, McCain by <strike>11</strike>5% (but on <strike>3</strike>12% reporting only)</p>\u000A<p>Massachusetts (93/43): Clinton by 16%, Romney by 12%</p>\u000A<p>Connecticut (48/30): Obama by <strike>3</strike>4% (not final), McCain by <strike>18</strike>21%</p>\u000A<p>Oklahoma (38/41): Clinton by 25%, McCain by <strike>10</strike>5% (but only 2% in)</p>\u000A<p>Arkansas (35/34): Clinton by 43%, Huackabee by 32%</p>\u000A<p>Montana (25):  McCain by 3% over Romney (9% counted)</p>\u000A<p>UPDATE2: McCain is shooting ahead. He now has 309 delegates to 99 for Romney. Much closer with Democrats with Clinton 279 to Obama 210.</p>\u000A<p>Illinois (153/57): Obama by 29%, McCain by 23%</p>\u000A<p>New Jersey (107/52): Clinton by 32%, McCain by 30%</p>\u000A<p>Missouri (72/58): Clinton by 18%, Huckabee by 7%</p>\u000A<p>Alabama (52/48): Obama by 38%, McCain by 7% (only 23% counted)</p>\u000A<p>Delaware (15/18): Clinton by 2%, McCain by 7% (only 29% counted)</p>

VA correction and an apology
p884
sg5
Vhttp://norightturn.blogspot.com/2008/02/correction-and-apology.html
p885
sg13
(lp886
sg15
V<p>DPF <a href="http://www.kiwiblog.co.nz/2008/02/once_again_nrt_makes_it_up.html">accuses me of misrepresenting him</a> in my latest post on <a href="http://norightturn.blogspot.com/2008/02/climate-change-strapped-chicken.html">the BRT's strapped chicken</a>. And looking at it again, he's right.  DPF did not explicitly say that he regarded the BRT's bogus study as proof positive that we should do nothing about climate change; instead, he simply said it implicitly.  Clearly, I was utterly mistaken in drawing the obvious and invited conclusion from the statements "there is a tradeoff", "we must look at the costs and benefits", and "the costs are too high", and I apologise unreservedly for misrepresenting DPF as an honest man who might stand by what he says, rather than a crawling spindoctor who hides behind plausible deniability in an effort to dogwhistle denial.\u000A\u000A<p>Mea culpa, mea culpa, mea maxima culpa, and I look forward to DPF engaging with the actual substance of my post.
