VMy Worst of 2007: Waitangi Day Special Edition (The Leftovers)
p896
sg5
Vhttp://www.stuff.co.nz/blogs/blogonthetracks/2008/02/06/my-worst-of-2007-waitangi-day-special-edition-the-leftovers/
p897
sg13
(lp898
sg15
V<p>It\u2019s <a target="_blank" href="http://www.nzhistory.net.nz/politics/waitangiday-introduction"><strong>Waitangi Day</strong></a>. So I\u2019m going to make it easy \u2013 here are the remaining bad albums that I reviewed in 2007. I have already made a <strong><a target="_blank" href="http://www.stuff.co.nz/blogs/blogonthetracks/2008/01/16/my-worst-of-2007-new-zealand-edition/"><strong>Worst of 2007: New Zealand Edition</strong></a></strong> and a <a target="_blank" href="http://www.stuff.co.nz/blogs/blogonthetracks/2008/01/21/my-worst-of-2007-hip-hop-edition/"><strong>Worst of 2007: Hip-Hop Edition.</strong></a> Here are the leftovers, literally the scraps. The junk that infiltrated my stereo in and around some decent albums\u2026I think it\u2019s fun to revisit the nasty reviews. They\u2019re certainly fun to write, which is a good payoff when the album in question is not much fun to listen to. There are seven reviews here \u2013 all by artists that seem to have a rabid fan-base that took my reviews far too seriously. Anyway, hope you\u2019re having a day off work \u2013 I am, for once. So here\u2019s a final stroll through the worst of 2007.</p>\u000A<p><a target="_blank" href="http://www.amazon.com/Grand-National-John-Butler-Trio/dp/B000N3ST4S"><strong>The John Butler Trio<br />\u000AGrand National</strong></a></p>\u000A<p>Blame Ben Harper! Thanks to that slide-guitar charlatan we now have the antipodean version, replete with rope-head Rastafarian intentions and just brimming with earnest peace and love crap in his lyrics. Yup, John Butler is back \u2013 and with each and every album his fan base continues to grow. Good on him. His whole manufactured \u201Claidback approach\u201D (hey, it must be laidback if the dude plays guitar in a chair right?) gets on my nerves. JJ Cale\u2019s been strumming on the porch for years. No pretensions there. But Butler really grinds my gears with his hippie-dippie philosophy. He\u2019s the reverse of Mel Gibson \u2013 an American who wants to be Australian and wants to love all cultures, colours and creeds. At least Gibson, and I\u2019m not saying drunk-driving is cool, is being honest with who he really is. I heard most of the songs on <em>Grand National</em> debuted by Butler during his last tour. I hated them then, and they sound worse without a crowd to endorse his cod-reggae impersonations. There\u2019s no question the man can play his guitar, but on record he seems to want to hang back and be a Bob Marley figure for folk who think they\u2019ve unlocked the secret by reading The Secret.</p>\u000A<p><a target="_blank" href="http://www.rhapsody.com/linkinpark/14435697_minutestomidnight"><strong>Linkin Park<br />\u000AMinutes to Midnight</strong></a></p>\u000A<p>Linkin Park has always been awful \u2013 but at least, before, the band was genuinely original as well as being horrid. They made their name spearheading the Nu-Metal genre, mixing cornball rap with truly dire screaming and screeching over processed, rubbery guitars and passionless, metronomic rhythms. The music didn\u2019t even have an icy-cold heart that could be admired (Kraftwerk) it was just soulless and redundant. Remember those swinging cool compilations called <em>Music To Watch Girls By?</em> Linkin Park could well have called all of their albums to date <em>Music For Idiots To Drive Around To!</em> But now, with <em>Minutes to Midnight </em>the group commits the ultimate Nu-Metal no-no; they attempt to be taken seriously. Yes, lyrically, there has always been a cloying earnestness. But I assumed this band couldn\u2019t actually be for real. They had to be poking fun musically, right? Well, as we know, one should never assume. Linkin Park have now made asses of themselves for jumping bandwagons and attempting to deliver an emo/nu-metal album. Lyrics like \u201CI bring it out, bring it in deeper just to throw it away\u201D are about as close as Chester Bennington will ever get to winning a Pulitzer. And he still can\u2019t sing to save himself.</p>\u000A<p><a target="_blank" href="http://www.artistdirect.com/nad/store/artist/album/0,,4100652,00.html"><strong>Maroon 5<br />\u000AIt Won\u2019t Be Soon Before Long</strong></a></p>\u000A<p><em>Songs About Jane</em> made Maroon 5 in to huge pop stars \u2013 even though the album was released in 2002 and took until 2005 to really take off. That song <em>This Love</em> was catchy, but so is the common cold. Adam Levine\u2019s adenoidal voice and penchant for watery white-boy funk suggests some awful meeting of the minds between Counting Crows, Jamiroquai, Hootie &amp; The Blowfish and Live. Ew. But, people seem to love the sound. I struggle to see why, particularly on this sugary, sappy follow-up release. The first two songs will make Stevie Wonder bless his own visual impairment \u2013 or else surely he\u2019d instinctively reach out and slap Levine and band. From there, I waited for a sign \u2013 heck, even a tumbleweed! Something, anything \u2013 to break up the monotony. Awful lyrical clichés (\u201CI never knew perfection/until I heard you speak\u201D) slip in and around super-slick, veneer-sheen pop hooks. I could imagine this album being useful for people about to undergo surgery for testicular cancer; they\u2019d get an idea, instantly, of what it is like to go through life without, um, you know what\u2026</p>\u000A<p><a target="_blank" href="http://www.amazon.com/Memory-Almost-Full-Deluxe-Limited/dp/B000PMLFRU"><strong>Paul McCartney<br />\u000AMemory Almost Full</strong></a></p>\u000A<p>Sure, Sir Macca might well have fathered half of Brit-Pop, but that doesn\u2019t mean that I want to hear a 65-year-old dad-type singing about one night stands. Is this conscious reinvention in the wake of outliving his own hymn to becoming a doddering 64-year-old? Most of <em>Memory Almost Full </em>plays out like a farewell to Wings, rather than a nod to that other band he was in. I\u2019ve always been a fan of McCartney \u2013 his last three albums (a loose trilogy of sorts from 1997\u2019s <em>Flaming Pie</em> through 2001\u2019s <em>Driving Rain</em> to 2005\u2019s <em>Chaos and Creation in the Backyard</em>) were so strong. Chaos went back to Wings \u2013 specifically <em>Band on the Run</em>. Here, <em>Memory Almost Full</em> is a half-baked mix of <em>Back to the Egg </em>and <em>McCartney II</em>; two albums that I like very much \u2013 but they stand out of time, in their own strange late-70s/early-80s bubble; reactions to punk and new-wave that are simultaneously blissfully unaware of the new musical concepts from the time. This new album just, mostly, sounds weird, despite the fact that the old boy can still write some melodic gems when he wants to. This is certainly the first McCartney album that should have fans questioning his contemporary validity.</p>\u000A<p><a target="_blank" href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Libertad_(album)"><strong>Velvet Revolver<br />\u000ALibertad</strong></a></p>\u000A<p>I wanted to like this album a lot. I thought that their debut, 2004\u2019s <em>Contraband</em>, was pretty good. I have one issue with Velvet Revolver, and I know I am not alone in this most obvious thought process: here is a band that should be a dream hard rock act, but will likely stumble under the weight of expectations. I mean this is essentially the last decent lineup of Guns\u2019n\u2019Roses with the voice of The Stone Temple Pilots doing the Axl role. Well, <em>Libertad </em>kicks off well, attempting to answer critics and suggesting the band has found its own sound (that aural Holy Grail for any post-Zeppelin hard rock act). Alas, it all falls away two-thirds of the way through the album and we get wannabe Rolling Stones circa-<em>Sticky Fingers </em>and, inexplicably, a glammed-up cover of ELO\u2019s <em>Can\u2019t Get You Out Of My Head</em>. Fortunately, I have gotten Velvet Revolver out of my head \u2013 and more importantly away from my stereo. There\u2019ll be one more album from these guys, max. Let\u2019s face facts; they really are just the new Audioslave.</p>\u000A<p><a target="_blank" href="http://www.avclub.com/content/music/korn"><strong>Korn<br />\u000A(Untitled)</strong></a></p>\u000A<p>It is unlikely that even the yoof of today could like Korn at this point \u2013 because an 18-year-old in 2007 would have been five years old when Korn debuted; you know back when you hated them for being the pillar of the burgeoning nu-metal scene? Or you loved them because your parents and un-cool friends hated them? Since then, we have had Marilyn Manson add layers of irony and dress-up (horror-)showmanship to this area of metal. We have had Limp Bizkit take white-boy hip-hop-laced metal to its pop-chart illogical extreme. And we have had Rage Against The Machine reform, to show how desperate musicians milking one idea truly are. So what hope is there, now that there\u2019s no hype, for Korn? I never really liked them, truth be told. But, occupational hazard, I have been aware of every album. This is their worst. Jonathan Davis seems to think that just by wishing himself to be the new Trent Reznor it will happen. Newsflash Jonathan: don\u2019t try to be cool and introspective and all untitled while you\u2019re still getting a major label to write the cheques that your butt can\u2019t cash.</p>\u000A<p><a target="_blank" href="http://www.cduniverse.com/search/xx/music/pid/7450079/a/Circus+Diablo.htm"><strong>Circus Diablo<br />\u000ACircus Diablo</strong></a></p>\u000A<p>Just this week I heard the very comforting news that The Cult has reformed, which means that Billy Duffy will be able to forget all about Circus Diablo. At least he has that luxury. I won\u2019t be able to forget hearing this. Alas. I got to my prince (a new album by The Cult sounds good) but the taste of kissing this frog will last longer than the third album by Audioslave or the second album by Velvet Revolver. In fact it may last just as long as having to watch a few songs by the band Supernova at their Wellington gig last year. This latest pointless excuse for attempted hard rock superannuation sees Ricky Warwick of The Almighty and Billy Morrison of Camp Freddy combining with Fuel\u2019s Brett Scallions and The Cult guitarist Duffy to recycle riffs and come nowhere close to their former recorded glories. Proving that this was just a marketing exercise the band even drafted in the hard-rock drummer to the stars Matt Sorum (The Cult, Guns\u2019n\u2019Roses, Velvet Revolver \u2013 isn\u2019t that an ever decreasing circle?) Circus Diablo even opened for Velvet Revolver \u2013 Sorum getting Charles Ruggiero to sub for him for live gigs.</p>

VLiberalism and organisations
p944
sg5
Vhttp://newzealandconservative.blogspot.com/2008/01/liberalism-and-organisations.html
p945
sg13
(lp946
sg15
VWith traditionalist critics of liberalism such as <a href="http://ozconservative.blogspot.com/">Mark Richardson</a> persistently pointing out that the myth of the autonomous, self-authoring individual is one of keys to understanding liberal individualism, it's worth considering whether the principles of liberalism apply to organisations and societies as well.<br /><br />In the same way that liberal theory argues that individuals should be free to re-create themselves, according to their own whims and logic, liberal elites see themselves as being justified in continually changing organisations such as businesses, government departments and NGOs, according to rational criteria and liberal principles such as personal autonomy and egalitarianism.<br /><br />In the 19th Century, radical-liberal theorist Karl Marx noted the "bourgeois obsession with reform," which he attributed to the logical workings of capitalism. More recently, enlightenment critics such as <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_Ralston_Saul">John Ralston Saul</a> have pointed to the obsession western elites have with rational methodology, which they believe gives them the mandate to continually change and disrupt organisations, according to rational criteria, regardless of established customs, experience and common sense.<br /><br />In <em><a href="http://www.scottlondon.com/reviews/saul.html">Voltaire's Bastards</a></em>, Saul argued that one result of the hubristic belief in rational methodology, is that managers tend to be rewarded according to adherence to methodology rather than actual results, both in the public and private sectors. Similarly, the word <em>managerialism</em> has entered the English language to identify arrogant psuedo-technocrats, who value generic qualifications and skills over specific expertise and practical experience.<br /><br />Anti-managerialism has a growing intellectual following in Britain, thanks to the micro-management excesses of Nu Labour. One British blogger who writes quite frequently on managerialism is Chris Dillow, author of the blog <em><a href="http://stumblingandmumbling.typepad.com/">Stumbling and Mumbling</a></em>.<br /><br />The liberal nature of organisational reform in western countries is clearly apparent when western organisations are compared with those in other developed nations, such as Japan and Korea, which do not share the West's cultural history. Despite the unprecedented economic and technological change which Japan has experienced since 1945, the structure and habits of Japanese corporations have undergone relatively little change in the last 6o odd years.<br /><br />Highly successful firms such as Toyota and Sony continue to pay their senior managers modest salaries by western standards, and Japanese businesses still make many inexpensive, labour intensive products. By contrast, most western companies have long since shifted such manufacturing to the third world.<br /><br />Japanese firms are also cautious of egalitarian reforms such as opening-up management positions to women graduates and fast-tracing intelligent and ambitious graduates at the expense of experienced workers. Indeed, whole sectors of the Japanese economy, such as distribution and farming, are still largely run along traditional lines.<br /><br />Despite placing a high value on education, senior Japanese managers seem to put more emphasis on the importance of practical experience than their western counterparts.<br /><br />In contrast to the way organisations are conservatively managed in Japan, western organisations are subject to a whirlwind of change, to which many workers are increasingly numb.<br /><br />Diversity training, down-sizing, team-building exercises, political correctness, counseling, office-layout fads and incessantly changing business jargon are just some of the many questionable changes which today's western workforce is expected to put up with.<br /><br />Even organisations which are thought of as bastions of tradition, such as long-established churches, are subject to a level of change which would be unheard of in most cultures. The Church of England, for example, has been under considerable pressure to accept gay and female clergy as well as significant changes to its traditional religious services.<br /><br />The last 150 years have seen an enormous amount of change within western organisations, but the pace of change has intensified dramatically in the last 30-40 years, and an increasingly amount of that change has been of questionable practical benefit - which ties in with the intense degree of ideological social reform which has occurred in western society during this period.<br /><br />Given that most other cultures are very weary of such intense and rapid organisation change, the western managerial class may well be setting unrealistic expectations about how much anti-traditional change is possible or disirable.

VObama-file 10 Barack Obama and the Socialist "Mafia"
p970
sg5
Vhttp://newzeal.blogspot.com/2008/02/obama-file-10-barack-obama-and.html

VObama-file 9 <a href="http://newzeal.blogspot.com/2008/02/obama-file-9-us-communists-explain.html">here</a><br /><br />I'm sure most of my readers have seen Mafia funerals depicted on "<em>The Sopranos</em>" or "<em>The Godfather</em>" movies.<br /><br />The FBI is always there, photographing every dapper suited "<em>don</em>" and thuggish looking "<em>soldier</em>".<br /><br />In its war against the Mafia, the FBI knows that funerals are a great opportunity to learn more about the Mob's "<em>order of battle</em>", hierachy and internal relationships.<br /><br />Socialist funerals and memorial services can be a bit like that.<br /><br />In politics, as in other forms of crime, you may be judged by the company you keep.<br /><br />On March 13th 1998, Saul Mendelson, a lifelong socialist activist died in Chicago.<br /><br /><a href="http://bp3.blogger.com/_JtTfGekhAhY/R6PRvi_In8I/AAAAAAAABU8/BgEmh73-73Q/s1600-h/Saul2.jpg"><img src="http://bp3.blogger.com/_JtTfGekhAhY/R6PRvi_In8I/AAAAAAAABU8/BgEmh73-73Q/s200/Saul2.jpg" border="0" alt="" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5162200212672389058" /></a><br />Mendelson had been a member of various Trotskyist factions in the 1930s and '40s before joining the US Socialist Party.<br /><br />In 1958 Mendelson founded the <a href="http://www.chicagodsa.org/dthdin.html">Debs Dinner</a>, an ongoing annual event and highpoint of the Chicago socialist calendar.<br /><br />Over the years, the dinner has served as a focal point for Chicago's socialist, ex Trotskyist, ex-communist and left wing Democratic Party community.<br /><br />In 1983, many of the Debs Dinner crowd helped form a new Marxist organisation-<a href="http://newzeal.blogspot.com/2008/01/obama-file-7-barack-obama-and.html">Democratic Socialists of America </a>(DSA)<br /><br />The Debs Dinner crowd/DSA, <a href="http://newzeal.blogspot.com/2007/10/chicagos-redblack-alliance-targets.html">in conjunction </a>with the Communist Party, helped elect Chicago's leftist Mayor Harold Washington in 1983, Carol Mosely Braun to the US Senate in 1992 and Barack Obama to the Illinois State Senate in 1996 and to the US Senate in 2004.<br /><br />The same crowd <a href="http://newzeal.blogspot.com/2008/01/obama-file-3-socialist-unionists.html">continues to back </a>Barack Obama in his current bid for the US presidency.<br /><br />Saul Mendelson was a leader of the Chicago DSA and personally played a large role in the election of Harold Washington.<br /><br />The <a href="http://www.saulmendelson.com/memor329.html">Saul Mendelson Memorial Servi</a>ce was held on Sunday, March 29, 1998, at the First Unitarian Church, Chicago.<br /><br />According to Chicago DSA leader, <a href="http://newzeal.blogspot.com/2008/01/obama-file-7-barack-obama-and.html">Carl Marx Shier </a>(who addressed the gathering);<br /><br /><em>At the memorial service held at the 1st Unitarian Church on South Woodlawn, speaker after speaker recounted Saul's contributions. <br /><br />The service was ably MC'd by a retired colleague, Bob Clark. I spoke first and was followed by Saul's friend Deborah Meier, a MacArthur Genius Grant recipient who is now starting a new school in Boston. Amy Isaacs, National Director of the ADA, spoke of what Saul had meant on foreign affairs to the ADA. <br /><br />Other speakers included Senator Carol Moseley Braun, Alderman Toni Preckwinkle, State Senator Barak Obama, Illinois House Majority Leader Barbara Flynn Currie and a good friend from New York, Myra Russell. <br /><br />The concluding remarks were made by an old friend, Harriet Lefley, who is now Professor of Psychology at the University of Miami Medical School.</em><br /><br />Deborah Meier was a former Trotsyist and Socialist Party comrade of Saul Mendelson's and a leader of Chicago and Boston DSA.<br /><br />Amy Isaacs was national director of <a href="http://www.adaction.org/about.htm">Americans for Democratic Action</a>. In recent years ADA has been increasingly linked to DSA and the DSA initiated <a href="http://newzeal.blogspot.com/2006/12/progressive-caucus-to-dominate-new-us.html">Congressional Progressive Caucus</a>.<br /><br /><a href="http://newzeal.blogspot.com/2007/12/carol-moseley-braun-did-clinton-send-as.html">Carol Moseley Braun </a>was then a US Senator with strong links to both DSA and the Communist Party. Barack Obama helped get her elected in 1992 and then took over her old Senate seat in 2004.<br /><br />State Senator Barak Obama probably knew Saul Mendelson through his ties to the old communist/socialist infiltrated, <a href="http://www.iviipo.org/">Independent Voters of Illinois</a>, in which Mendelson played a leading role.<br /><br />Alderman Toni Preckwinkle and Illinois House Majority Leader Barbara Flynn Currie, are both leftist Democrats with ties to Chicago's socialist community. Both endorsed Barack Obama in his successful 2004 bid for the US Senate.<br /><br />Harriet Lefley was a Trotskyist in the 1940s with Saul Mendelson.<br /><br />Eulogies also came from Quinn Brisben, (Socialist Party presidential candidate 1976, 1992) and David McReynolds (Socialist Party presidential candidate 1980, 2000).<br /><br />Both Brisben and McReynolds are also members of DSA.<br /><br />Ten short years ago, Barack Obama was up to his ears in the Chicago socialist mafia.<br /><br />Like the criminal mafia, the socialist version gets want it wants through fraud and other covert means. Deception and underhand political maneuvrings are the socialists stock in trade.<br /><br />The US wouldn't want a president who had ties to the criminal mafia.<br /><br />Why would they want a president with links to the socialist "<em>mob</em>"?<br /><br />Obama-file 11 <a href="http://newzeal.blogspot.com/2008/02/obama-file-11-communists-muster-latino.html">here</a>

VPork Barrel roads
p982
sg5
Vhttp://libertyscott.blogspot.com/2008/02/pork-barrel-roads.html
p983
sg13
(lp984
sg15
V<div align="justify">In the 1980s and 1990s, funding for roads in New Zealand moved away from a pork barrel approach to one based on several key principles:</div><div align="justify">1.   All central government funding for roads sourced from taxes raised from road users (with an increasing proportion of such taxes dedicated to such funding);</div><div align="justify">2.   Removing direct political interference on decisions regarding which projects would proceed and would not proceed by appointing boards with specific independence to fund and develop projects that would meet goals such as economic efficiency and safety, within available budgets;</div><div align="justify">3.   Allocating funding for projects based upon advancing those with the best ratio of benefits to costs first, and delaying/deferring very high cost projects with relatively marginal benefits.  In short, allowing spending to be concentrated on maintenance and smaller projects that could be cost controlled, and allowed steady improvements to networks;</div><div align="justify">4.  Increasing road funding based upon steady growth of funds for new projects, not largescale increases that could place severe pressure on contracting costs.</div><div align="justify">~</div><div align="justify">Since 1999 Labour has eroded these principles, significantly by:</div><div align="justify">1.  Introduced specific Crown taxpayer votes of funding for transport projects, in addition to dedicated road tax based funding (albeit it has also dedicated more and more road taxes to transport as well);</div><div align="justify">2. Introducing far more specificity in the outputs that the Minister of Transport expects from the crown agencies funding and building roading networks, and becoming significantly more interested in the timing of major road projects, particularly in Auckland;</div><div align="justify">3. Placing pressure on the government appointed boards to advance projects based upon "strategic considerations", being code for advancing lower value projects with high political profiles over higher value projects with lower political profiles.   None of this is explicit or public, but it involve phone calls to board chairs, conversations between politicians, board members and chief executives;</div><div align="justify">4.  Allowing goldplating and greenplating of major state highway projects with little justification based upon quantifiable returns or benefits (e.g. tunnel under Victoria Park viaduct), but high political profile.   </div><div align="justify">5.  Engaging politically driven official groups for special funding of transport in Auckland, Wellington, Bay of Plenty and Waikato to buy regional political support, and advance low value high cost projects that fail following the changes listed above.    </div><div align="justify">~</div><div align="justify">The last time you saw it explicitly was when Labour bought Winston Peters by using taxpayer funds to advance the Tauranga HarbourLink project, even though all the work beforehand indicated it could have been easily funded through tolls.    </div><div align="justify">~</div><div align="justify">Now you see it with <a href="http://www.stuff.co.nz/4390442a19715.html">Dr Cullen about to bribe Auckland voters with their tax cut </a>- but by funding a heavily greenplated, expensive, and not particularly efficient new motorway.   This project has grown from around NZ$700 million in cost to well over NZ$1 billion, and its benefit cost ratio has always hovered below 1:1.   It cannot be funded from tolls as Transit's own analysis indicates motorists wouldn't pay to use it.   On top of that, while it could be built as a motorway at surface (with some noise barriers), what is being proposed, largely for an environmental argument (i hesitate to use the word reason), is a huge tunnel, adding enormously to the cost.   Before you say "it's done in Sydney", Sydney isn't a big volcanic basin - tunnelling is easy and cheap there, it isn't in Auckland.  </div><div align="justify">~</div><div align="justify">"but we need the road" you say?  Well, prove it.   Two other segments of the SH20 motorway are under construction now, extending it east towards the southern motorway bypassing Manukau and west towards Mt Roskill.  Both of these projects are good, and will make a big difference to traffic conditions around Auckland.   When completed they may indicate there is demand for improved roads between Mt Roskill and Waterview, and then?   Well, let the private sector finance and build the road, find a route, develop a design,  buy properties as necessary and then IT can toll it (and it would be fair for the proportion of fuel tax and road user charges paid when using the road are paid from the government to the owner).    Why should current taxpayers (not road users) fund a road that will be used for generations?  Why not let it be financed and the debt paid off over time from charges by those who will use it?  </div><div align="justify">~</div><div align="justify">It wont happen?  Well maybe the road isn't that necessary then.   Getting the government's state highway agency (Transit) with an insatiable appetite to spend money, to contract yet another huge road project in Auckland, right now, will further inflate road contracting costs.   Promises from the contracting sector that funding lots of roads at once will save money have proven nonsensical.   </div><div align="justify">~</div><div align="justify">So I'd let Transit fiddle around with determining a route, but that's about it - and finish the other two major projects on that corridor (plus duplicating the congested Mangere bridge, by tolling the new lanes).    Then Dr Cullen you can give New Zealanders a bigger tax cut.  Instead of spending $1.5 billion on a motorway of dubious economics, you might give that money to New Zealanders - $375 per man, woman and child would do a lot of good, wouldn't it?</div>

In the week when the tenth Kiwi was slain in the month of January, the public are clamouring for solutions to crime and Annette King the Police and Justice Minister who was touring the street of a double shooting bizarrely said that it was the hot weather and the full moon that was the cause of all the&nbsp;mayhem.\u000A</p>\u000A<p>\u000APerhaps it isn't really a surprise that the public thinks Clark' labour Government is soft on crime. Is it any wonder when photo's like this of her smiling while young gang members flip gang signs. Yes the photo is old, but I bet none of us have seen it in the <span class="caps">MSM</span>. Some of us even missed it <a href="http://theyworkforyou.co.nz/portfolios/corrections/2007/aug/21/o01#3" target="_blank" rel="nofollow">being mentioned in parliament,</a>  but mentioned it was and glossed over by an inept Corrections&nbsp;Minister. \u000A</p>\u000A<p>\u000AWell unfortunately for Clark, I have a copy of it and have placed it in my Really Truly Helen Gallery. Every time there is a crime spree or shooting, or mugging I am going to reminder her of her fondness for young thugs by posting the photo. I have even thought of making a billboard of the shot and putting it somewhere like Manurewa or Waitekere or Botany or anywhere else that crime has become the number one reason for resident <span class="caps">NOT</span> to vote&nbsp;Labour.\u000A</p>\u000A<p>\u000ALabour on Waitangi day appears broken, dejected and breft of anything meaningful for New Zealand. It isn't really a surprise when the Prime Minister poses with young thugs smiling like a crocodile as they flip gang signs is&nbsp;it?\u000A</p>\u000A<p>\u000ALabour is soft on&nbsp;Crime. \u000A</p>

VWeb 3.0: Is It About Personalization?
p1080
sg5
Vhttp://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/readwriteweb/~3/229484823/web_30_is_it_about_personalization.php
p1081
sg13
(lp1082
sg15
V<p><img border="0" src="http://www.readwriteweb.com/images/web30logo.jpg" width="150" height="60" />On the UK's Guardian newspaper site today, writer Jemina Kiss suggested that Web 3.0 will be about recommendation.  "If web 2.0 could be summarized as interaction, web 3.0 must be about recommendation and personalization," <a href="http://www.guardian.co.uk/media/2008/feb/04/web20?gusrc=rss&feed=media">she wrote</a>.  Using Last.fm and Facebook's Beacon as an example, Kiss painted a picture of a web where personalized recommendation services can feed us information on new music, new products, and where to eat.  It's a marketers dream and it's really not far off from the definitions we've come up with in the past here on ReadWriteWeb.</p>\u000A\u000A<p>We've written about web 3.0 and attempted to define it many, many times here over the past year.  One of the common themes between almost all of the posts is that Web 3.0 and the vision of the Semantic Web are joined at the hip.</p>\u000A\u000A<p>Last April, we held a contest asking readers for their <a href="http://www.readwriteweb.com/archives/define_web_30_contest_winners.php">web 3.0 definitions</a>.  Our favorite came from <a href="http://www.outofrhythm.com/">Robert O'Brien</a>, who defined Web 3.0 as a "decentralized asynchronous me."</p>\u000A\u000A<p>"Web 1.0: Centralized Them. Web 2.0: Distributed Us. Web 3.0: Decentralized Me," he wrote. "[Web 3.0 is] about me when I don't want to participate in the world. It's about me when I want to have more control of my environment particularly who I let in. When my attention is stretched who/what do I pay attention to and who do I let pay attention to me. It is more effective communication for me!"</p>\u000A\u000A<p>What O'Brien was getting at is basically what Kiss was getting at: personalization and recommendation.  And that's the promise of the Semantic Web.  The easiest way to sell the Semantic Web vision to consumers is to talk about how it can make their lives easier.  When machines understand things in human terms, and can apply that knowledge to your attention data, we'll have a web that knows what we want and when we want it.</p>\u000A\u000A<p>ReadWriteWeb contributor Sramana Mitra put it another way on this blog last February, when she said that web 3.0 will be about <a href="http://www.readwriteweb.com/archives/web_30_4cpvs.php">adding context to personalization</a>.  "Personalization has remained limited to some unsatisfactory efforts by the MyYahoo team, their primary disadvantage being the lack of a starting Context," she wrote.  "In Web 3.0, I predict, we are going to start seeing roll-ups. We will see a trunk that emerges from the Context, be it film (Netflix), music (iTunes), cooking / food, working women, single parents, ... and assembles the Web 3.0 formula that addresses the whole set of needs of a consumer in that Context."  Or in other words, web 3.0 will be about feeding you the information that you want, when you want it (in the proper context).</p>\u000A\u000A<p>Of course, the versioning of the Internet is kind of silly, and probably shouldn't keep going, but it is a fun way to look to the future and predict what we might be coming our way.  What do you think of Kiss's idea about web 3.0 being about recommendation and personalization?</p>\u000A<p><a href="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~a/readwriteweb?a=UCFCfz"><img src="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~a/readwriteweb?i=UCFCfz" border="0" /></a></p><div class="feedflare">\u000A<a href="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~f/readwriteweb?a=XNWdDTE"><img src="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~f/readwriteweb?i=XNWdDTE" border="0" /></a> <a href="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~f/readwriteweb?a=bmN0SyE"><img src="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~f/readwriteweb?i=bmN0SyE" border="0" /></a> <a href="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~f/readwriteweb?a=b8a2wie"><img src="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~f/readwriteweb?i=b8a2wie" border="0" /></a> <a href="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~f/readwriteweb?a=bG9aPPe"><img src="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~f/readwriteweb?i=bG9aPPe" border="0" /></a> <a href="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~f/readwriteweb?a=RGhpWKe"><img src="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~f/readwriteweb?i=RGhpWKe" border="0" /></a> <a href="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~f/readwriteweb?a=0lD6rjE"><img src="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~f/readwriteweb?i=0lD6rjE" border="0" /></a> <a href="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~f/readwriteweb?a=ySkV05E"><img src="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~f/readwriteweb?i=ySkV05E" border="0" /></a>\u000A</div><img src="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/readwriteweb/~4/229484823" height="1" width="1" />

V<p>Phil Goff has done well. A US-NZ free trade agreement is now a real possibility with the announcement that the <a href="http://www.nzherald.co.nz/section/3/story.cfm?c_id=3&objectid=10490783">US will begin negotiations</a> with the P4 group of NZ, Brunei, Chile and Singapore.</p>\u000A<p>This doesn't mean a full free trade deal is guaranteed.  For now it only covers financial services and investments, but is has the potential to morph into a more comprehensive negotiation. VThe Pacific trash vortex
p1195
sg5
Vhttp://norightturn.blogspot.com/2008/02/pacific-trash-vortex.html
p1196
sg13
(lp1197
sg15
V<p><img src="http://www.independent.co.uk/multimedia/archive/00015/05RubbishGraphic_15022a.jpg" />\u000A\u000A<p>The <i>Independent</i> today has a piece on the <a href="http://www.independent.co.uk/environment/the-worlds-rubbish-dump-a-garbage-tip-that-stretches-from-hawaii-to-japan-778016.html">Pacific trash vortex</a>, a vast area of the North Pacific which (thanks to a current system called the <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/North_Pacific_Gyre">North Pacific gyre</a>) has become a floating trash dump.  But not just any trash - most stuff that ends up in the oceans biodegrades or sinks long before it makes its way to the gyre.  Instead, this area is full of our longest-lasting waste: plastic. An estimated 100 million tons of it, forming a soup that stretches from Hawaii to Japan.  Here's a description of the trash vortex from a piece on the <a href="http://www.bestlifeonline.com/cms/publish/travel-leisure/Our_oceans_are_turning_into_plastic_are_we.shtml">pastic ocean</a>:\u000A<blockquote>\u000A<i>It began with a line of plastic bags ghosting the surface, followed by an ugly tangle of junk: nets and ropes and bottles, motor-oil jugs and cracked bath toys, a mangled tarp. Tires. A traffic cone. Moore could not believe his eyes. Out here in this desolate place, the water was a stew of plastic crap. It was as though someone had taken the pristine seascape of his youth and swapped it for a landfill.</i>\u000A</blockquote>\u000A\u000AThe basic problem is that plastic is both light (or rather, dense) enough to float, and also essentially immortal.  Nothing eats plastic.  It's not broken down by the environment, except by physical processes which grind it into plastic dust ("biodegradable" plastic bags simply break down into smaller pieces of plastic).  So, it just piles up.  And unfortunately its piling up in the oceans.  This isn't just ugly - it's also a threat to the marine food chain.  Macroscopic plastic items such as bottletops and pens may be mistaken for food and eaten by fish and marine animals.  As plastic is indigestible, this is - eventually - fatal (there's a picture of the results at the top of <a href="http://www.naturalhistorymag.com/master.html?http://www.naturalhistorymag.com/1103/1103_feature.html">this article</a>).  Microscopic fragments are eaten by plankton, with the same result.  But worse, plastics attract and concentrate complex organic pollutants like PCBs - meaning that our dumping of plastic in the oceans is slowly poisoning our food chain.  According to <i>The World Without Us</i>, there has already been one study correlating ingested plastics with PCBs in the fat tissue of puffins.  And there will likely be more as people start looking.  In short, plastics and chemical polluants are a toxic combination, and we're slowly poisoning ourselves with them.\u000A\u000A<p>What can we do about this?  Recycle, for one (though that's not particularly effective, as thanks to low melting temperatures you can't safely make new plastic bottles out of old ones).  Reduce usage as well (plastic supermarket bags are convenient, I know.  But they're also a long-lasting problem).  But most of all, <i>clean up after yourself</i>.  Don't let this shit get in the oceans.

VHilzoy on Hardheaded Idealism
p1207
sg5
Vhttp://www.philosophyetc.net/2008/02/hilzoy-on-hardheaded-idealism.html
p1208
sg13
(lp1209
sg15
VAfter detailing substantive reasons for supporting Obama (see also <a href="http://www.philosophyetc.net/2008/01/reasons-for-obama.html">my old post</a>) Hilzoy <a href="http://obsidianwings.blogs.com/obsidian_wings/2008/02/obama-actually.html">concludes</a>:<br /><blockquote>I sometimes wonder why, exactly, people go on saying all this stuff about Obama lacking substance. Sometimes, I suspect it's just laziness, as in the case of this dKos story in which mcjoan, who is usually much better than this, lists a whole lot of questions she wishes the candidates would answer, apparently unaware that Obama (and, for all I know, Clinton), has already answered most of them. I suspect, though, that part of it might be the assumption that idealism is necessarily woolly and misty-eyed and all about singing Kumbaya, while realism is necessarily cynical and disillusioned.<br /><br />I have never believed this. There are certainly hard-bitten, cynical people who don't think particularly clearly about the world (Dick Cheney leaps to mind.) More to the point, I can't see any reason why there shouldn't also be people who are both genuinely idealistic and hardheaded at the same time. I suspect Obama is one of them. I do not for a moment imagine that he is perfect. (Cough, clean coal technology, cough cough.) But I do think that he's one of the best candidates I can remember, and that's good enough for me.</blockquote><br />Do read the whole thing, though. The details are important, and not the sort of thing that's covered in our dumbed-down mainstream media.<div class="feedflare">\u000A<a href="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~f/PhilosophyEtCetera?a=ohf9JPE"><img src="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~f/PhilosophyEtCetera?i=ohf9JPE" border="0" /></a> <a href="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~f/PhilosophyEtCetera?a=7hNvBwE"><img src="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~f/PhilosophyEtCetera?i=7hNvBwE" border="0" /></a> <a href="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~f/PhilosophyEtCetera?a=xvgT6ae"><img src="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~f/PhilosophyEtCetera?i=xvgT6ae" border="0" /></a>\u000A</div>

VSitting Dunedin South MP David Benson-Pope will likely spend the next few months looking for a new career, after losing the 2008 Labour Party nomination to local PR woman Clare Curran over the weekend.<br /><span>Quelle demage.</span><div><img src="http://www.davegeeonline.com/blog/08/02-05-dncurran.jpg" height="200" width="160" /></div>Curran, an elected Labour Party official, has been involved with the union movements in both Australia and New Zealand in recent years. She currently runs a small public relations/communications business in Dunedin with her partner.<br /><br />However, Clare Curran is more well known to the general public as the "woman who was awarded an uncontested contract with the Environment Ministry", at the request of Labour MP David Parker (Climate Change minister).  She was also described by his Private Secretary as Parker's "right-hand woman".<br /><br /><a href="http://www.tv3.co.nz/VideoBrowseAll/PoliticsVideo/tabid/370/articleID/45028/cat/67/Default.aspx#video">TV3's coverage of the Dunedin selection result was rather ominous...</a> "The coffin lid is closing on the political career of David Benson-Pope"...<br /><br /><div><img src="http://www.davegeeonline.com/blog/08/02-05-dbptrio.jpg" height="184" width="404" /></div><br />Benson-Pope said after the 2005 election campaign that he thought media coverage of him was "way over the top", and that reporters and interviewers at both TV One and TV3 were "downright rude really".<br /><br />DBP has been the Labour MP for Dunedin South for almost nine years, following a period as a Labour Dunedin city councillor. VPalestinians could change Gaza
p1335
sg5
Vhttp://libertyscott.blogspot.com/2008/02/palestinians-could-change-gaza.html
p1336
sg13
(lp1337
sg15
V<div align="justify">It should hardly be a surprise that recent coverage by the so-called peace loving left about Gaza retains a remarkable willingness to be blind to what the \u201Cgovernment\u201D in Gaza did to provoke Israel into sealing off its border.  <br />~<br />Let me remind you.   Israel withdrew from Gaza in 2005.  Withdrew, that\u2019s right pulled out as it has been asked since 1967.   It has no governance or military presence on this strip of land whatsoever.    It has removed the 9000 or so Jewish settlements, it has essentially done exactly what all of its opponents asked of it, regarding Gaza.   Now some argue that as Israel still controls the airspace, territorial waters and the borders with Israel that there is not complete control, but still, it is sovereign territory notwithstanding that.</div><div align="justify"><br />The Palestinian authority elections in 2006 saw Palestinian voters have a set of odious choices.  The main ones were either vote for Fatah, which supports peaceful co-existence with Israel, but has proven itself highly corrupt and administratively incompetent, or vote for Hamas, which wants to destroy Israel, but also has run schools, medical centres and tends to be far less prone to corruption.   There were <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Palestinian_legislative_election%2C_2006#Parties_participating">other parties offering alternatives </a>that were not Islamist and with no background on corruption.   Some of these could have provided a more reformist way forward, but no they chose Hamas.   By choosing Hamas, Palestinian voters chose war with Israel.<br />~<br />Without going into the detail about Hamas being effectively ousted from power in the West Bank, it remains that Hamas governs Gaza.   Israel\u2019s withdrawal means it is effectively the government of a rump Palestinian state of sorts.   What did Hamas do with this power?  It started firing rockets into Israel proper \u2013 you know, the country that is a UN member state, recognised by the vast majority of countries around the world including Egypt and Jordan.   Hamas decided that it was more worthwhile to attack Israel than to try to rebuild the shattered infrastructure and economy of Gaza, blighted by conflict over decades.  Why?  Because Hamas has little interest in the here and now, but every interest in fighting the \u201Cinfidels\u201D.<br />~<br />With over 4,000 rockets hitting Israel,  Israel could, on the basis of self defence, have reoccupied Gaza to root out those attacking it.   It has not.   What it has done is impose economic sanctions against the Hamas regime (Western countries including New Zealand have imposed such sanctions against countries that never laid a hand on it), built a barrier around Gaza (Israeli side not Egyptian) to restrict entry by terrorists into Israel, and put up a blockade against most imports that could aid and assist those attacking Israel.   It has also attacked from the air, sites from where rockets are being launched.  <br />~<br />If you listened to the views of Israel\u2019s critics it should have done none of this, but sit back and watched its people\u2019s homes be bombarded from a territory that Israel does not control.   It is notable that Egypt hasn\u2019t much tolerated the onslaught of Palestinians on its border either, but nobody blames Egypt do they?<br />~<br />Gaza, of course, is in an appalling state.   It has high population density (though lower than the likes of Hong Kong and Singapore), under developed and hardly a haven of prosperity.    Hamas could change that of course.   </div><div align="justify">~</div><div align="justify">It could stop attacking Israel and announce that Gaza will not be a base for attacks on Israel.   It might find economic sanctions get lifted.   It could seek to be outward looking and encourage Palestinians to seek trade as the way forward, and presumably their wealthy allies in Saudi Arabia might cough up some of their funds to finance simple infrastructure such as water, sewage, roads and electricity.   Of course they wont, because keeping Palestinians in poverty, angry and willing to fight to regain Jerusalem is exactly what their rich friends want.   The Palestinians are, in some respect, waging a proxy war for Iran and Saudi Arabia, one that makes them the losers.<br />~<br />In other words, there is a chance for Gaza to, with some effort, be transformed.   It is on a stretch of land that could become an attraction for tourists, it has horticulture and could become a free trade area, if only Hamas would also set up an independent judiciary that could enforce private property rights and contracts.   <br />~<br />I doubt whether it will, of course.   You see Hamas worships the afterlife, being Islamists.   It cultivates a culture that worships violence, celebrates death and honours those who give their lives to take those of others.   It actively recruits the young to sacrifice their lives for this cause of violence.  </div><div align="justify">~</div><div align="justify">Gaza could be so much more than a strip of hell.    Remember, Israel withdrew \u2013 it doesn\u2019t want it back \u2013 Palestinians have it, and they wont get Israel proper \u2013 ever.   If Gaza could succeed, then it would have positive effects on the West Bank, as Palestinians no longer act as victims, but set up a haven of prosperity, freedom and peace.   Doing that will open borders with Israel (and the world) more than any militancy ever could.</div>

VMySpace Platform Aims to Pick Up Where Facebook Left Off
p1387
sg5
Vhttp://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/readwriteweb/~3/229360211/myspace_platform.php
p1388
sg13
(lp1389
sg15
V<p><img src="http://www.readwriteweb.com/images/myspaceplatlogo.jpg" />MySpace is launching its <a href="http://developer.myspace.com">developer platform</a> tomorrow and is going great lengths to highlight the ways it's different from the Facebook Platform.  That's ironic given that the dominant reaction to the Facebook Platform, from users at least if not the press, is that it's made the site too much like MySpace.</p>\u000A\u000A<p>None the less, there are some very interesting details available about the MySpace Platform.  After all, that is where the action is - <a href="http://www.readwriteweb.com/archives/myspace_still_kicking.php">there's far more traffic to MySpace than Facebook</a>.</p>\u000A\u000A<p>A few highlights concerning the announcement include:<br />\u000A<ul><li>The best part of the announcement, as far as I'm concerned, is that MySpace apps will be allowed to include user admin/home page interfaces in addition to the part of the app that displays on the public facing profile your friends see.  It will be drag and drop, making your admin page a lot like an AJAX start page.  This is a big differentiator with Facebook so far.</li><br />\u000A<li>Developers will have one month to work on apps for the platform before users come in.  It's open to all, something MySpace says will "democratize" the process and prevent any early-access favoratism given to a handful of select companies on the Facebook Platform.</li><br />\u000A<li>User security is high priority and apps will be limited in their ability to access information.  Some critics allege that this is not the case at all over on Facebook, saying the Platform there gives total access to any app allowed to enter your profile.  That said, see our earlier post today on MySpace and Google.</li><br />\u000A<li>There are three APIs, the Google-lead OpenSocial being the primary one, some MySpace extensions for fields like favorite movies is another.  Though we've said that OpenSocial would be better described as OpenWidget, this instance at least will support social graph portability. Notable.  Note also though that this is one more platform deploying "OpenSocial - Plus."  Get enough Plusses in a room together and you have to wonder how much anyone is communicating with anyone else.</li><br />\u000A<li>MySpace's <a href="http://oauth.net">oAuth</a> support, via OpenSocial, will - I believe - make MySpace by far the biggest user of oAuth on the web.  That's great news for this open standards based authentication protocol.  More oAuth = more and safter mashups all around the web.</li></ul></p>\u000A\u000A<p>The least convincing reply to my questions came when I asked MySpace CTO Aber Whitcomb what would keep MySpace apps from being as annoying as the ones that have lead Facebook users to complain that Facebook is now too much like MySpace.  Whitcomb said that MySpace apps would be less annoying because developers would have more and equal time to develop them, this next month before users let in, and so there would be fewer trivial and poorly made apps.</p>\u000A\u000A<p>Finally, I'd just like to add to this discussion that MySpace has solved the spam issue better than almost anyone else on the web.  Have you noticed?  At the end of September <a href="http://www.readwriteweb.com/archives/myspace_captchas.php">MySpace installed a Captcha requirement</a> before a friend request could be sent and I feel like I haven't gotten a single spam request since then.  That's great!</p>\u000A\u000A<p>You can be snobby about your friends' noisy MySpace pages and the "classier" Facebook experience if you want, but many people are getting tired of the Facebook Platform already and it will be interesting to see what the leading social network online can do now.</p>\u000A<p><a href="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~a/readwriteweb?a=SBVk3m"><img src="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~a/readwriteweb?i=SBVk3m" border="0" /></a></p><div class="feedflare">\u000A<a href="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~f/readwriteweb?a=T28RWDE"><img src="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~f/readwriteweb?i=T28RWDE" border="0" /></a> <a href="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~f/readwriteweb?a=Cw26OaE"><img src="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~f/readwriteweb?i=Cw26OaE" border="0" /></a> <a href="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~f/readwriteweb?a=ZXDML3e"><img src="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~f/readwriteweb?i=ZXDML3e" border="0" /></a> <a href="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~f/readwriteweb?a=17mBnre"><img src="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~f/readwriteweb?i=17mBnre" border="0" /></a> <a href="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~f/readwriteweb?a=UW0TaQe"><img src="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~f/readwriteweb?i=UW0TaQe" border="0" /></a> <a href="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~f/readwriteweb?a=4PKzMnE"><img src="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~f/readwriteweb?i=4PKzMnE" border="0" /></a> <a href="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~f/readwriteweb?a=nPMDRmE"><img src="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~f/readwriteweb?i=nPMDRmE" border="0" /></a>\u000A</div><img src="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/readwriteweb/~4/229360211" height="1" width="1" />

V<p>After enjoying Maori support for Labour for decades, Helen Clark <a href="http://www.nzherald.co.nz/event/story.cfm?c_id=1500878&objectid=10490738">no longer visits Waitangi</a> on February 6, because in 1998, Maori activist Titewhai Harawira made her cry, and in 2004 she was 'jostled'.</p>\u000A<p>After Brash's Orewa speech, Maori hated National.  Yet after a <a href="http://www.stuff.co.nz/4153371a6442.html">simple and effective visit</a> to a predominately Maori Auckland street, John Key has captured Maori hearts and minds.  This year he rocked up to Waitangi with Helen's nemesis Titewhai Harawira.  Then he entered the meeting house and <a href="http://tvnz.co.nz/view/page/411749/1571973">shook Tame Iti's hand</a>.</p>\u000A<p><a href="http://pacificempire.org.nz/wp-content/uploads/2008/02/6pm_waikey_050208_232.jpg" align="center" title="6pm_waikey_050208_232.jpg"><img src="http://pacificempire.org.nz/wp-content/uploads/2008/02/6pm_waikey_050208_232.jpg" alt="6pm_waikey_050208_232.jpg" align="middle" /></a></p>\u000A<p>Let me me rephrase that.  He walked up to the leader of the Urewera 17, who were <a href="http://pacificempire.org.nz/2008/01/22/violence-is-a-virtue-why-the-urewera-17-were-a-genuine-threat/">'allegedly' plotting to assasinate Key himself</a> - <strong>and shook the man's hand.</strong></p>\u000A<p>Let's review.<br />\u000A<strong><br />\u000AWaitangi Day, February 6.</strong></p>\u000A<blockquote><p> <strong>Clark:</strong>  <em>Cries and refuses to come back.</em><br />\u000A<strong><br />\u000AKey:</strong><em> Strolls in and shakes the hand of the <strong>man who plotted to kill him</strong>.</em></p></blockquote>\u000A<p>Key may not have policies, but he sure has balls!</p>

VFutureCar shows great talent & technology, so what's wrong at General Motors?

V<div><p><img alt="FutureCar" hspace="5" src="http://rcd.typepad.com/personal/FutureCar.png" align="right" vspace="5" border="0" />I&rsquo;ve just watched FutureCar&nbsp;which features many designers, and car companies, but is largely focused on General Motors. VA menu of rotten fish
p1462
sg5
Vhttp://tumeke.blogspot.com/2008/02/menu-of-rotten-fish.html
p1463
sg13
(lp1464
sg15
V<a href="http://bp3.blogger.com/_Yu6lJst3lkM/R6g5Wx7G91I/AAAAAAAAAQI/0DwqS2qEkN0/s1600-h/ngati_porou_takutaimoana.jpg"><img src="http://bp3.blogger.com/_Yu6lJst3lkM/R6g5Wx7G91I/AAAAAAAAAQI/0DwqS2qEkN0/s400/ngati_porou_takutaimoana.jpg" border="0" alt="" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5163440036301436754" /></a><a href="http://www.beehive.govt.nz/release/foreshore+and+seabed+heads+agreement+ng\u0101ti+porou+11">Government press release</a> for:<br /><br /><center>HEADS OF AGREEMENT BETWEEN NGA HAPU O NGATI POROU AND THE CROWN</center><br /><br />Firstly: <i>The negotiations are being conducted in accordance with section 96 of the Foreshore and Seabed Act 2004.</i><br />- so Ngati Porou now accept the confiscation act.  Simple as that - no weasel words - they accept it, that is the pre-condition for the negotiations.<br /><br /><i>The Heads of Agreement aims to:<br />\u2022 recognise the unbroken, inalienable and enduring mana of the hap\u016B of Ngati Porou in relation to the <b>public foreshore and seabed</b> in their rohe...</i><br />- and they must accept that the lie perpetrated in the confiscation act that it is "public" (ie. Crown-owned) and not theirs.<br /><br /><span>The agreement describes eight instruments through which the mana of the hapu of Ngati Porou, in relation to the <b>public foreshore and seabed</b> in their rohe, would be recognised at law <b>in a way that is consistent with the object of the Foreshore and Seabed Act.</b>...</span><br />- the object being the confiscation of their property.  So they have to beg these would-be colonial masters for a quasi-waiver of the confiscation act provisions only so long as the original unjust, racist intent of the act - the act condemned in the UN report amongst others - is adhered to.  That is the basis of the deal.<br /><br /><i>1. A <b>Statutory Overlay</b> that recognises the special status [...] is recorded in key public documents such as district and regional plans and statements and is taken account of in consent processes under the Resource Management Act and the Marine Reserves Act.</i><br />- "notification" and "participation" in process only.<br /><br /><span>2. An <b>Environmental Covenant</b>, which will ensure that statutory plans prepared and administered by Gisborne District Council conform to a statement by Ng\u0101ti Porou on the sustainable management of natural and physical resources.</span><br />- the Gisborne District Council must "recognise and provide for the Environmental Covenant" in territorial customary rights areas and only "take into account" the covenant in all other areas. But any change due to it "will follow the normal public notification processes under the Resource Management Act 1991." - meaning it can be objected to presumably.<br /><br /><span>3. <b>Relationship Covenants</b> between the hapu of Ngati Porou and a number of Ministers</span><br />- perhaps funniest of all. They actually have the nerve to see this as some form of special acknowledgement.  Ha! Whopdee shit, a bit of face time with a minister.  The miners and the Tally Bros will get more time with the government players without any formal understandings of what courtesy amounts to. "The Crown will also write to the following agencies to encourage them to enter into relationship instruments with Ng\u0101ti Porou: Gisborne District Council and Transit New Zealand." That's right, they'll write a letter to them!  Talk about padding.<br /><br /><span>4. A <b>Fisheries Mechanism</b> that will allow Fisheries Management Committees to develop customary fisheries resource management plans and subsequent regulations (made by the Minister of Fisheries)</span><br />- this is all under the 1996 Fisheries Act anyway, so it's more smoke and mirrors and the illusion of concessions, but get this: if the minister, once the public have had their say (of course) determines "an undue adverse effect on existing fishing interests" ie. Pakeha or commercial interests then... computer says 'no'.<br /><br /><span>5. A <b>Wahi Tapu protection mechanism</b> that will give the supporting hapu the right to restrict or prohibit access to wahi tapu and wahi tapu areas within the public foreshore and seabed in their rohe.</span><br />- yeah, because tapu areas are public aren't they?  How can a tapu area be in a public area? Because the government made it public by the confiscation act so that they then have to <strike>negotiate</strike> beg for it to be recognised as tapu again from that much weaker position of having to establish that its origins "pre-date 1840" and the other "evidentiary" tests that the confiscation act stipulate.<br /><br /><span>6. A <b>protected customary activities mechanism</b> that will allow the supporting hapu the right to continue carrying out specified customary activities without resource consent in or on the public foreshore and seabed in their rohe.</span><br />- and here we start seeing this phrasing: <i>"The requirement for the relevant hapu to give approval for resource consent applications that may have a significant adverse effect on a protected customary activity does not apply to <b>certain accommodated matters."</b></i>  Whatever that means.  It is important because it potentially undoes this clause.  Oh, and once again, it's all in terms of the confiscation act's provisos anyway. Cullen has stated many times that all he considers this clause to mean is launching waka and collecting hangi stones.<br /><br /><span>7. A <b>pouwhenua instrument</b> that will give the hapu of Ngati Porou the right to erect Pouwhenua at culturally significant sites </span><br />- a form of boundary marker, but in this instance it has nothing more than "cultural significance".  It isn't allowed to mean anything to the Crown that would imply ownership by Ngati Porou.<br /><br /><span>8. A <b>placenames instrument</b> that will officially recognise traditional names or alter names of culturally significant areas.</span><br />- well, once again whoopee!  That would have happened anyway "in accordance with the New Zealand Geographic Board Act 1946."<br /><br /><span>Where specific territorial customary rights are recognised as part of this agreement the hapu signing this agreement will also have the following additional protections within those territorial customary rights areas:<br />\u2022 A Permission Right instrument that will provide the right to approve or withhold approval for any resource consent...<br />\u2022 An extended Fisheries Mechanism that provides the signatories with the ability to make by-laws under customary fishing regulations...<br />\u2022 An extended Environmental Covenant, which gives the signatories the ability to ensure all statutory plans that cover a territorial customary rights area recognise and provide for the approach of the hap\u016B to the sustainable management of physical and natural resources in that areas.</span><br />- well now that final bit sounds like we're getting somewhere. But once again the "Permission Right does not apply to certain <i>accommodated matters</i>" etc. etc.  It's all in the details and that has yet to be determined.<br /><br /><span>Once ratified, appointed representatives of [Ngati Porou] will file an application in the High Court for confirmation that the requirements for a finding by the High Court under section 96 of the Foreshore and Seabed Act have been satisfied.  Legislation will also be required to give effect to the Deed of Agreement once the territorial customary rights areas have been confirmed by the High Court.</span><br />- so all the rigmarole of the tilted playing field that the confiscation act created must still be gone through anyway.  Anyway.  Like what's the diff?  Not much at all it seems.<br /><br />As Harvey Keitel says in the beer ad "what you say 'no' to - defines you."  The mana of Ngati Porou leadership is on the line here along with the whole tribe (or at least the 40 of the 51 sub-tribes).  They aren't saying 'no' to the confiscation act.  And by extension they are saying 'no' to Maori solidarity.<br /><br /><b>------------UPDATE--------------</b><br />Watching Maori TV's flagship <i>Te Kaea</i> news programme I just heard the cross-eyed presenter, Scotty, exclaim at the end of the piece about the signing of the deal at parliament "Kamo te wehi! Ngati Porou" ("Awesome stuff, Ngati Porou") WTF!  Awesome is it, Scotty?  Try kupapa te wehi, Scotty. It's not just his eyesight that's all screwed up.  Why doesn't he just wear a Labour party badge while he's at it. Unbelievable.  Where was the critique from the Maori Party that the Pakeha networks had... you know... balance?  Don't they exist?  What's going on at MTS?  Is H2 running it on behalf of the PM?  Is their funding in jeopardy if they don't help the government?  Are they run by pro-Labour hacks?  I was going to make a pitch to put their news service online, but why would I want to transfer a Labour Party love-in onto the internet.  Ditch that idea. Very disappointing.  I'll have to keep a closer eye on them from now on.

V<a href="http://bp1.blogger.com/_Yu6lJst3lkM/R6elQh7G90I/AAAAAAAAAQA/PwNpTThvGE4/s1600-h/derek_fox_credit_dominionpost.jpg"><img src="http://bp1.blogger.com/_Yu6lJst3lkM/R6elQh7G90I/AAAAAAAAAQA/PwNpTThvGE4/s200/derek_fox_credit_dominionpost.jpg" border="0" alt="" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5163277201206343490" /></a><a href="http://www.nzherald.co.nz/section/1/story.cfm?c_id=1&objectid=10490680">NZH reports deal on foreshore confiscation</a>.  I've just seen the pictures on TV of Cullen cuddling up to the Ngati Porou leadership.  This Iwi have been portrayed as kupapa (traitors) for their historic and continuing collaboration with the Crown - and this exercise will merely confirm that status in the minds of many observers.  Their thinking that they can get more out of the Crown by breaking solidarity with other tribes is unprincipled and the outcome highly questionable. If they think they will get anything substantially more than the "White Man's Touch" as the Crown determined property test for their own land, and the "White Man's Word" as the Crown determined process of over-riding that property test then they are in dreamland.  And if by a divine miracle they do get anything more than that then it automatically destroys all credibility the government has in having passed the raupatu in the first place. They keep voting for Horomia after all, what does that say about their political acumen?<br /><br />On that score I hope <a href="http://www.stuff.co.nz/4387308a6160.html">Derek Fox kicks his arse.</a>  He got within 695 votes last time he stood - and will be odds on to take the seat off Horomia should he be nominated by the Maori Party.  The party's nominations from what I've gathered:<br /><br /><i>Candidate Selection Progress<br /><br /><b>Hauraki - Waikato</b><br />Selection  hui were held over a two week period in Pukekohe, Hamilton , Matamata, Huntly, Manurewa, Paeroa and Raglan.  On 27 November, Angeline Greensill was elected as the candidate to contest Hauraki-Waikato for the Maori Party.<br /><br /><b>Te Tai Tonga</b><br />Nominations opened on the 17th December 2007..  Nominations close on the 14th January 2008 (next Monday)..   Selection Hui will be held from the 10th - 15th February 2008<br /><br /><b>Ikaroa Rawhiti</b><br />Nominations opened on the 1 January 2008.  Nominations close on the 31st January 2008.  Selection Hui will be held from 2-8 March 2008.</i><br /><br />The Maori seats could all go their way if they continue to conduct themselves with vigour and independence over the next months.<br /><br />As for a National Party - Maori Party deal, yes it is possible, but only if the foreshore confiscation law is repealed.  That is the deal-maker/deal-breaker.  As my co-blogger mentioned this morning and as I have stated many times since the issue erupted in 2003: public access to all foreshore and seabed regardless of what property status it has is what is important to the public. Confiscating every square millimetre off Maori whilst protecting Pakeha rights in the same category so that Pakeha can get 80% of aquaculture areas and can build marinas etc. which over-rides Maori property, customary and other rights  will never be accepted because it is unconstitutional, unjust and racist.  We didn't need the UN to tell us that in their report because we already know, the government knows, Maori know, everyones knows: a Pakeha-run government can and will screw over Maori for as little a reason as mere bureaucratic convenience.  If Ngati Porou wants to attempt to bargain with a regime that treats them as <i>abos</i> instead of boycotting them and returning a staunch MP who will keep those bastards honest - then more fool them.  They are playing the divide-and-rule game by which all Crown governments have successfully managed to undermine the autonomy and protection that the Treaty afforded the communities that consented to it.<br /><br />As for the Nats - it is consistent with their property rights agenda and their pragmatism that they take that Maori Party deal.  Key must keep the red necks in his caucus in check to achieve it.  Not an easy task with characters like McCully and Nick Smith etc. etc. lurking in the shadows waiting for their opportunity to stumble out, voice their 1950s reactionary and racist venom and promptly lose the un-lose-able election.<br /><br /><b>---------UPDATE 6:30pm---------</b><br />In the <a href="http://www.beehive.govt.nz/release/foreshore+and+seabed+heads+agreement+ng\u0101ti+porou+11">government press release</a> Cullen's quoted as commending "the good faith and sincerity with which Ng\u0101ti Porou have approached these negotiations" - which others might well characterise as a commendation of their ability to sell-out - to do their bidding, to play their game, to tow their line, to dance to their tune and fulfil their role as a bit player in Labour's manipulations of the Maori electorate.  <i>Praise from Caesar is an indictment indeed; when the world stands against that man and his greed.</i> To the negotiators they would doubtlessly think they are getting a good a deal as they can, but the timing especially is all carefully choreographed to Labour's agenda of "good news" leading up to Waitangi Day.<br /><br />On Radio New Zealand I'm hearing Tariana Turia reminding Dr Mahuika (a lead negotiator for Ngati Porou) of his original opposition to the confiscation bill and that negotiating with the Crown is a reversal of that policy.  (Of course by accepting the Crown's bullshit framework inside of the Act breaks the solidarity against it.)  Cullen says the agreement will be put into legislation - which will be a publicly dissected humiliation rather than any re-assertion of Ngati Porou mana - because we will all see just how little they get and how much they think they are worth.  And because Horomia is tangata whenua we'll see how this deal pans out for him in his constituency as it is presumed by him and Labour that it will be seen as him "delivering" and "walking the talk" and all those other stupendous waffly jabbered buzz-words that he spouts. And who, upon hearing Dr Mahuika's comments on One News tonight about the Maori Party, would say he is anything other than a Labour Party stooge?<br /><br />So what have they signed up to? - I'll post the critique once I've gone through the two documents issued today and <a href="http://www.beehive.govt.nz/release/foreshore+and+seabed+heads+agreement+ng\u0101ti+porou+11">available as word doc's</a> on the govt. website.

VPodcasting Becoming More Popular, Advertisers Take Notice
p1481
sg5
Vhttp://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/readwriteweb/~3/229484824/podcasting_becoming_more_popular.php
p1482
sg13
(lp1483
sg15
V<p><i>This is a guest post by Aseem Kishore, a technology enthusiast and lead blogger for <a href="http://www.online-tech-tips.com/">Online-Tech-Tips</a>.</i></p>\u000A\u000A<p><img src="http://www.readwriteweb.com/images/podcast_feb08.jpg" />The US podcasting market has steadily been increasing in size over the last couple of years and is expected to double within the next two years to almost 38 million people, <a href="http://www.emarketer.com/Article.aspx?id=1005869&src=article1_newsltr">according to eMarketer</a>. With these kinds of numbers, podcasters and advertisers are starting to look into ways to generate more revenue through video ads.</p>\u000A\u000A<p>It is estimated that the total US podcast audience for 2007 is 18.5 million with an active podcast audience of 6.5 million. The 18.5 million number refers to individuals who have ever downloaded a podcast from anywhere. The "active" user base refers to individuals who have downloaded an average of one or more podcasts per week.</p>\u000A\u000A<p>The active podcast audience is expected to grow to an impressive 25 million listeners by 2012 and advertisers are expected to spend close to $450 million by 2012.</p>\u000A\u000A<p>There are many reasons why podcasting is becoming more popular in the US at such a fast rate. Firstly, podcast content is easy to digest. Most podcasts that are downloaded are usually short and focus on specific topics or genres, making it easy for people to listen to exactly what they are interested in and skip the fluff. With professional high-quality content and no commercials, it's easy to see why people may prefer to view a podcast over a TV show.</p>\u000A\u000A<p>Also, there is a much greater awareness and much more promotion for podcasting via large online news and media networks such as CNET, New York Times, and well-respected blogs <em>[Ed: see our own <a href="http://readwritetalk.com/">ReadWriteTalk</a> for example]</em>. Podcasts have also become part of many people's daily lives thanks to Apple's iPod and iTunes. With iTunes and the vast numbers of iPods, users are able to instantly and easily download podcasts onto their PC's or iPods, making watching a podcast almost as normal as listening to an MP3.</p>\u000A\u000A<p>Following the success of Apple's iTunes, other major players have released portable media players that can play podcasts - such as Microsoft's Zune player and the Zune Marketplace - thereby increasing the podcast audience.</p>\u000A\u000A<p>On top of that, there has a been a prediction that within four years 40% of all video viewed will be outside of the television set. That's coming from a poll carried out by Jack Meyers and tracked by the firm Teletrax of 300 media executives.</p>\u000A\u000A<p>The key questions will be whether the growth of the podcast audience will continue to increase at the current rate and will it be enough to attract large amounts of ad spending. Most podcasters make money through advertising on the pages/feeds that distribute the podcast, as well as embedding ads into the podcast itself. Sponsorships and subscription services are not as popular, but will grow as the podcasting market increases. </p>\u000A<p><a href="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~a/readwriteweb?a=HCuKr1"><img src="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~a/readwriteweb?i=HCuKr1" border="0" /></a></p><div class="feedflare">\u000A<a href="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~f/readwriteweb?a=7xj5ihE"><img src="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~f/readwriteweb?i=7xj5ihE" border="0" /></a> <a href="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~f/readwriteweb?a=muYKqWE"><img src="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~f/readwriteweb?i=muYKqWE" border="0" /></a> <a href="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~f/readwriteweb?a=Bumh08e"><img src="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~f/readwriteweb?i=Bumh08e" border="0" /></a> <a href="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~f/readwriteweb?a=RRSZnoe"><img src="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~f/readwriteweb?i=RRSZnoe" border="0" /></a> <a href="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~f/readwriteweb?a=b72MC7e"><img src="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~f/readwriteweb?i=b72MC7e" border="0" /></a> <a href="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~f/readwriteweb?a=secBKzE"><img src="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~f/readwriteweb?i=secBKzE" border="0" /></a> <a href="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~f/readwriteweb?a=cS9NQLE"><img src="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~f/readwriteweb?i=cS9NQLE" border="0" /></a>\u000A</div><img src="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/readwriteweb/~4/229484824" height="1" width="1" />
